# 212 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Conversation on the Movie the Day after Viewing the Movie

**Rational aim**
To enable students to articulate their learning from the movie.
To have some idea of where to go for help when affected by alcohol.

**Experiential Aim**
To care about the effects of alcoholism and know that others care.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Let's look back at the film we saw yesterday. Sometimes it's easier when we have had a little time to think about it.

**Objective Questions**
What do you remember today that was in the film?

**Reflective Questions**
What did you feel while you were watching the video?
What scene or part of the video made you feel like that?
What were you reminded of in your own life?

**Interpretive Questions**
What was this film about for you?
What did you learn from this film?

**Decisional Questions**
What can you do to get help when you are in a situation like this?

**Closing**
You have created your own mandalas as you drew your pictures in the circles yesterday. We will laminate these and return them to each of you for use as a personal place mat to keep in your own desk or to take home.

## 페이지 226 (SKU-000671170_11_00226.jpeg)

# Keeping Friends and Having Fun while Staying out of Trouble

*Creative Applications 213*

---

## Situation
Students see a video on trouble situations where drugs or alcohol are made available to students, and different ways that they refuse them. The students brainstorm trouble situations that they might encounter, then work on refusal skills. These skills are modeled and practiced, then role-played by the students. After the role-plays, the entire class engages in the following reflective questions.

**Rational Aim**
To be able to use different refusal skills appropriately in real life.

**Experiential Aim**
To be committed to refusing drugs and alcohol.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Wow, this was a busy day. Let's see if we can remember all that we did.

**Objective Questions**
What activities did we do today?

**Reflective Questions**
How did it feel to role-play?
What did you learn from the role-play you were in?

**Interpretive Questions**
What did you learn from another role-play?
What difference do these skills make in your life?

**Decisional Questions**
What shall we put on posters to remind us of these skills?
How will you personally remember these skills?
How will you use them?

**Closing**
Saying no when it is necessary is not easy, but I am confident that you will be able to do it. You are strong, and now you are skilled.

---

## 페이지 227 (SKU-000671170_11_00227.jpeg)

# 214 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Celebrating Community

### Situation
This final session with the class focuses on their life together as a class. They review and reflect upon their experiences of being a community, to close the year's curriculum.

**Rational Aim**
To provide an opportunity to reflect on personal growth and learning about taking care of ourselves.
To connect class learning with everyday life.

**Experiential Aim**
To be aware of personal changes and learnings.
To have the capacity to take new awareness into daily life and make wise choices.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
We have had a very interesting year together as a community of people in this classroom. As a class, you are a supportive community and can help each other to take care of yourselves. Let's reflect on the year from this perspective.

**Objective Questions**
What are words and pictures around the room which remind you of this community?

**Reflective Questions**
What were your feelings in the beginning of the year as you got to know each other?
How do you feel different now?

**Interpretive Questions**
What does learning all about healthy people, coping, and refusal skills have to do with *taking care of ourselves*?

**Decisional Questions**
What does your art work tell you about yourself?
What will you do to take care of yourself now, after all we've learned here?

**Closing**
Let's stand in a circle and thank one another for being the supportive community we are for one another. Your teacher is there for you, and will give help and feedback to you. As a class, you are a supportive community and can help each other to take care of yourselves.

---

## 페이지 228 (SKU-000671170_11_00228.jpeg)

# Creative Applications 215

## Conversations Linked with Other Tools

*Nunavut Inuuqatigiit Leadership Workshop*

This event, which includes a series of conversations and workshops, was designed to be done with Inuit school leaders from across the new territory of Nunavut. All participants speak one or more Inuit languages as well as English.

The first day focused on culturally appropriate learning, and the next several days focused on school leadership.

---

## Successful Learning in a Culturally Appropriate Way

### 표 요약

**Rational Objective:** 개인적인 Inuit 문화의 학습 방식과 공통 패턴에 대한 심층적 이해

**Experiential Aim:** Inuit 학습자로서 자신감과 강점 습득

**THE CONVERSATION - Opening (Welcome and context)**

- 파트너를 선택해 이름, 출신지, 생일, 진정으로 배운 경험을 나누는 소개 활동
- 두 사람의 이름을 작은 카드에 적기
- 벽 지도에 파트너를 소개하고 실로 장소 연결하기
- 진행자가 작업 가정 제시 (모든 사람은 지혜를 가짐, 틀린 답 없음, 전체는 부분의 합보다 큼)
- 진행자가 학교 밖 학습 개인 이야기 공유 (예: 할머니께 쿠키 만들기 배우기)
- 플립차트 또는 소그룹용 종이에 질문 작성
- 소그룹으로 나누어 편한 언어로 대화 진행

## 페이지 229 (SKU-000671170_11_00229.jpeg)

# 216 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Conversation on Learning in Small Groups

| **Rational Objective** | **THE CONVERSATION** |
|---|---|
| To have a deepened understanding of one's own personal learning styles and learning patterns common to Inuit culture | |
| **Experiential Aim** | |
| To gain strength & confidence as an Inuit learner | |

### Opening
In a minute we will split up into small groups to talk about our learning experiences. Please talk in any language you are comfortable with. Answer the following questions and bring back some stories, common elements, and underlying factors to share with the whole group.

### Objective Questions
- What are some events/times when you really learned something? Or you observed learning?
- These may be outside school, inside school, or a traditional skill.
- What did you learn?
- How did you learn?
- Who/what was the teacher if there was one?

### Reflective Questions
- What parts of these sound like the most fun?
- What parts sound difficult, painful or boring?

### Interpretive Questions
- What are common elements of successful learning in your stories?
- Summarize these common elements, and write them down.

### Decisional Questions
- What are the underlying factors that make learning successful for you? List them.
- These ideas might help you think of underlying factors:
  - A quiet environment? Noisy?
  - Moving around? Still?
  - Being alone? With others?
  - Visual images? Lots of words? Sounds or talking?
  - Others?

### Closing
It's time to take our work back to the whole group.

---

## 페이지 230 (SKU-000671170_11_00230.jpeg)

# Whole Group Reflection on Reports and Conversation on Learning

---

**Rational Objective**
To have a deepened understanding of one's own personal learning styles and learning patterns common to Inuit culture.

**Experiential Aim**
To gain strength & confidence as an Inuit learner.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Each team reports uninterrupted.

Reports: Each group shares their stories, common elements of successful learning and really important underlying factors in successful learning.

**Objective Questions**
What words caught your attention as you heard these reports?

**Reflective Questions**
What made you laugh?
Where did you think, "Oh, yeah, I understand that!"
What images came to mind?

**Interpretive Questions**
What patterns did you hear? — Where did you hear more than one group say the same thing?
Which factors are the most important? Which were said the most times?
Drawing together what you've heard, what elements are there when successful learning is going on? *(Write on flipchart.)*

**Decisional Questions**
Imagine that academic learning and cultural learning are in two separate boxes.
Drop the boxes, leaving two piles of kinds of learning. Now move the piles of learning together.
What might all that we've learned here mean for learning and for a school based on Innuqatigiit, or Inuit cultural learning (i.e. geometry out on the land, or teamwork in solving problems)?
This conversation is followed by a consensus workshop *(see the Appendix for procedures)* with the focus question "What do we want to see in a place of learning (school) that supports successful Inuit culturally appropriate learning?"

---

## 페이지 231 (SKU-000671170_11_00231.jpeg)

# 218 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Leadership Conversations

| **Rational Objective** | **THE CONVERSATION** |
|---|---|
| To have a deep understanding of leadership that works in this culture. | |
| **Experiential Aim** | |
| To gain hope that leadership is possible, and to have a glimpse of selves as leaders. | |

### Opening
First let's reflect for a moment on our experience of yesterday's work on successful learning:
- What do you recall from yesterday? *(Objective)*
- Where did you have an "Aha!"? *(Reflective)*
- What is one thing you learned yesterday that is useful to you? *(Interpretive)*
- What is your commitment to successful learning? *(Decisional)*

### Opening
Let's step back a bit: When I say the word *Leadership:…*

### Objective Questions
What's the first image that comes to mind?

### Reflective Questions
What's your gut level reaction?

### Interpretive Questions
What are some of the things that real leaders do?
What responsibilities do leaders have?

### Decisional Questions
Summarize what we've said — what do leaders do?

# Conversations on Leadership in Small Groups

*Creative Applications 219*

---

## Rational Objective
To have a deep understanding of leadership that works in this culture.

## Experiential Aim
To gain hope that leadership is possible, and to have a glimpse of selves as leaders.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
Now let's have conversations in small groups again.
At the end of the conversation, bring back qualities of successful leadership to share with the whole group.

### Objective Questions
Each person tells a story.
What are some times you've seen real leadership going on?
In the camp?
In the community?
In the school?

### Reflective Questions
What do you like most about being a leader?
What is difficult about being a leader?
What kinds of leadership make you uncomfortable?

### Interpretive Questions
What common elements are there in your stories?
What are some of the qualities of successful leadership?

### Decisional Questions
How would you summarize the qualities we have discovered?

## 페이지 233 (SKU-000671170_11_00233.jpeg)

# 220 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Reflections on Reports and Conversation on Leadership with the Whole Group

### 왼쪽 열

**Rational Objective**
To have a deep understanding of leadership that works in this culture

**Experiential Aim**
To gain hope that leadership is possible, and to have a glimpse of selves as leaders

**Hints**
Sometimes conversations that follow each other directly do not have a separate closing. The closing of one conversation and the opening statement of the next may be the same sentence.
Procedures for the consensus workshop method referred to here can be found in the Appendix.

**Other Applications**
Reflecting on how we learn does not have to be in a culturally specific context. Sometimes we get caught up in traditional expectations of teaching others, without reflecting on our experience of successful learning. One or two of these conversations might be an interesting way to start a year, or to introduce an inservice session on learning styles.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
We want to hear reports now from each group, including a story and a summary of the qualities of successful leadership you identified. Let's hear one report after the other, without any interruption.

**Objective Questions**
As you heard these reports, what words caught your attention?

**Reflective Questions**
What was really exciting?
What were you reminded of by someone else's report?

**Interpretive Questions**
Which of the qualities you heard would you pick out as key qualities of leadership in Inuit culture?

**Decisional Questions**
What might this mean for leadership in a place of learning (school) based on Inuuqatigiit?
This conversation is then followed by three consensus workshops:
- A vision for leadership in schools (places of learning),
- Obstacles to that vision, and
- Strategies to deal with the obstacles and realize the vision.

---

## 페이지 234 (SKU-000671170_11_00234.jpeg)

# Debrifing a Cross-Cultural Simulation Game

*Creative Applications 221*

---

## Situation

Students in a university class in Japan are preparing for a trip abroad. They start with a cross-cultural simulation game called *BaFá-BaFá*, created by Simulation Training Systems. This is a powerful game, and a lengthy debriefing discussion is essential to processing emotions and sharing insights.

---

## 표/도해 요약

**Rational Aim**
- 언어가 유일한 소통 방식이 아님을 보여줌
- 문화의 숨겨진 차원 이해
- 다양한 배경의 사람들과 만날 준비
- 문화 간 유사점과 차이점 비교

**Existential Aim**
- 문화 충격 경험 및 감정 표현
- 다른 문화의 다양한 가치 인식

**Hints**
- 처음 두 단계는 게임 직후, 나머지 두 단계는 일주일 후 저널 작성 후 진행 가능
- 총 시간: 60~90분

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
Let's stand back from this experience for a little while and debrief our experience.

### Objective Questions
*(Beta/Alpha persons 간 상호 관찰 및 규칙 분석 질문 포함)*

### Reflective Questions
*(다른 문화 방문 시 감정, 상호작용, 즐거움 관련 질문 포함)*

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 235 (SKU-000671170_11_00235.jpeg)

## 222 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

### Whole Group Debriefing Discussion *(continued)*

What part was most difficult or confusing?
How do you feel about your own culture (Alpha or Beta)?

**Interpretive Questions**
Which country would you like to live in? Why?
What are some of the values of the Alpha culture? The Beta culture?
What did you discover about yourself?
What did you find out about intercultural communication?

**Decisional Questions**
How will this experience affect you when you travel abroad?
How will this affect the way you communicate with visitors here in Hokkaido?
If you do your visit over again, what would you do differently this time?

**Closing**
*Reflection Papers:*
Following the group discussion, participants are asked to write a reflection on their experience in their journals. A short form for a few paragraphs of writing and a long form of several pages have been designed. The students are asked to be conscious of their own changes that occurred during and after the game.
The following is a list of the interpretive level questions used for the short homework assignment: Write one paragraph about the following questions:

- What did you know about yourself that you didn't know before the game?
- What did you learn about intercultural communication that you didn't know before?
- How do you think this knowledge or experience will help you in the future?

## 페이지 236 (SKU-000671170_11_00236.jpeg)

# Journal Writing after the Experience of the Simulation Game

---

## 표 구조 요약

### 좌측 컬럼

**Situation**
Participants are given a written assignment to reflect on their experience after a cross-cultural simulation game.

**Rational Aim**
To probe the experience of a cross-cultural simulation game.
To be more aware of personal values.

**Experiential Aim**
To wrestle with unexpressed values.

**Hints**
The simulation game can be done in about 90 minutes followed by 45-60 minutes of discussion. If done over several days, an extended three-session schedule can be done.

---

### 우측 컬럼: THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Write four to six pages of your reflections in a journal during the next week concerning the *BaFá-BaFá* simulation game. Here are some questions to answer in your writing.

**Objective Questions**
Recall: What happened?
What did you see?

**Reflective Questions**
How did you feel during the simulation? When did you feel that?
When did you feel confused?

**Interpretive Questions**
What did you learn about visiting another culture?
What did you learn about yourself?
What did you learn about intercultural communication that you didn't know before?

**Decisional**
How do you think this knowledge or experience will help in the future?

**Closing**
Write a poem or draw a picture that describes your experience of the whole game.

*Creative Applications 223*

## 페이지 237 (SKU-000671170_11_00237.jpeg)

# 224 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Complex Use of the Four Steps

### *Discussing an Incident in a Justice Circle Conferencing Process*

**Situation**

In New South Wales, Australia, an urban public school with a large Aboriginal and multicultural population has been working with the police to develop restorative justice processes. These justice circles allow students to deal with minor and major offences, involving their families, friends, and others in the process of conflict resolution, healing and behavioral change.

---

## Formal Justice Circle Conferencing Process

**[표/도해 요약]**

**Rational Aim:** To bring healing and closure to harm caused in the school setting

**Experiential Aim:** To have all concerned in a specific incident own the behavior, experience the pain caused, and have the possibility of making restitution and moving on.

**Hints:** Note that each "party" is asked objective, reflective, and interpretive questions before the conversation moves to the next person. The decisional level is asked to both victim and offender at the same time. These levels are indicated with O, R, I, and D before the questions. Involvement in the process pre-supposes a willingness on the part of all participants to attend, and that the offender has admitted his/her actions. Participants may include supporters of both victim and offender (e.g., parents, fellow students, relevant school staff, a community person/friend, where appropriate).

**Welcome.**

Introduce each participant and their relationship to the victim and offender.

We want to explore in what way people have been affected, and how we can work towards healing the harm that has been done.

*1. Facilitator to Offender/s:*
- O - Can you tell us what happened, and how you came to be involved?
- R - What were you thinking about when this happened?
- R - What have you thought about since?
- I - Who was affected? How?
*(Be sure offender owns the action)*
*2. Facilitator to Victim/s:*
- O - Can you tell us what happened?
- R - How did you feel at the time?
- R - How did you feel afterwards?
- I - How has this incident affected you? What has been hard for you?
- I - What did your friends/family think?

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 238 (SKU-000671170_11_00238.jpeg)

# Formal Justice Circle Conferencing Process *(continued)*

---

## 좌측 사이드바

Numbers should be kept to a minimum, and include only people key to the restitution process for the young people concerned.

This formal process may take one to three hours. It should be emphasized that it is important to take the necessary time to work through the issues with the students involved.

### Other Applications

This can be used in other community settings where punitive justice may be seen to be counterproductive. Often when an offender is able to see the impact of their behavior, that behavior may change.

---

## 우측 본문

**3. Facilitator to Victim's supporters:**
- O - What did you hear about this?
- R - How did you feel? What has been the hardest thing for you?
- I - What has happened since?
- I - What are the main issues for you?

**4. Facilitator to Offender's Supporters:**
- O - What did you hear about this?
- R - How did you feel? What has been the hardest thing or you?
- I - What has happened since?
- I - What are the main issues for you?

**5. Facilitator to Offender:**
You've heard from *(victim)* and *(supporters and/or family)*.
- I - Is there anything you want to say?

**6. Agreement — Facilitator to victim and then to victim supporters:**
- D - What would you like to see happen out of this?
*(Allow discussion time about possible reparation)* There may need to be some guiding questions here.

**Facilitator to offender:**
- D - Is there anything you want to say to… (victim?)
- D - Is there anything you should do to make things right?
- D - What do you think about what victim & supporters have said? How is it fair?

**Facilitator to offender's supporters, and then to all:**
- D - How is this fair?
- D - What is our agreement about how we will close this?

It is important that we clarify what has been agreed here….

*(Repeat agreement for confirmation. Invite any other comments where appropriate. Thank participants and invite to stay for refreshments. Informal time is important.)*

---

## 페이지 239 (SKU-000671170_11_00239.jpeg)

# 226 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Informal Version of the Justice Process

### THE CONVERSATION

**Objective Questions**
- What happened?

**Reflective Questions**
- What were you thinking about at the time?
- Who has been affected?
- How were they affected?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What's been the hardest thing for you?
- What have you thought about since?

**Decisional**
- What needs to happen now?

**Closing**
Thank you for your thoughtfulness and willingness to solve this. Let's go do it. More — acknowledgement, thanks, etc.

# Unusual Applications of the Four Levels of the Process

*Conversation on a Web Site for Students*

**Situation**
After the first election in Nunavut, the new Inuit territory of Canada, a newspaper ran an article about the election. Elementary students were asked to discuss the conversation on a website, accessible to students in schools across the territory of Nunavut.

**Other Applications**
Of course the questions in this conversation can be done live in class on news articles, as well.

---

## A News Article on the Nunavut Election

**[도해 요약: "Nunavut Election Guided Response" 웹사이트 화면]**

5개 섹션으로 구성된 안내 응답 화면:
1. The Globe & Mail 기사 읽기 (2-16-99)
2. 기사에서 언급된 사실 / 주목을 끈 한 가지 내용 작성
3. 기사가 어떤 감정을 느끼게 했는지 (행복, 슬픔, 화남, 자랑스러움, 두려움)
4. 기사에서 가장 중요한 것
5. 누나부트 선거에 관한 기사를 쓴다면 어떤 제목을 붙일지

## 페이지 241 (SKU-000671170_11_00241.jpeg)

# Four-Level Procedures for Interviewing Students to Resolve a Schoolyard Fight

*(228 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS)*

---

## 상황 (Situation)

뉴저지 학교에서 교사가 싸운 두 학생을 교장실로 데려옴. 두 학생은 교장 책상 앞에 서서 동시에 말하거나 침묵함. 교장은 학생들을 지도하는 중.

**Rational Aim:** 문제 해결 및 재발 방지 방법 학습

**Experiential Aim:** 경청받는 경험, 문제 해결 책임 수용

**Hints:** 반성 단계 말미에 한 명이 악수를 위해 손을 내미는 경향이 있음. 상대방이 준비되지 않을 수 있으므로 멈추고 설명할 것. 변화는 반성 단계 이후에 시작될 수 있음.

---

## 대화 구조 (The Conversation)

| 단계 | 내용 요약 |
|------|-----------|
| **Opening** | 조용히 서로 마주 보게 함 |
| **Objective Level** | A가 B에게 자신의 버전 설명, B는 경청. 이후 역할 교대 |
| **Reflective Level** | B가 먼저 감정 나눔. 번갈아 이야기, 교장과 나머지 한 명은 침묵 |
| **Interpretive Level** | 이번 일로 무엇을 배웠는가? A부터 시작, 번갈아 발언 |
| **Decisional Level** | B부터 시작: 이런 상황에서 다음엔 어떻게 할 것인가? |
| **Closing** | "서로 경청하고 배운 것이 자랑스럽다. 책임감 있는 학생들이다. 이제 가서 즐겁게 지내라." |

---

## 페이지 242 (SKU-000671170_11_00242.jpeg)

# Using the Four Steps in a Presentation: A Directive by a Principal on an Urgent Issue

---

## 표/도해 요약

**왼쪽 패널 (상황 및 목표)**

- **Situation**: 학생 양육권 관련 긴급 상황 발생. 기밀 정보 포함, 학교 법적 책임 및 아동 안전 문제
- **Rational Aim**: 직원들이 교장의 결정 이유를 이해하도록
- **Experiential Aim**: 직원들이 결정을 신뢰하고 실행하도록
- **Hints**: 토론이 아닌 연설 형식. 교장이 대화 구조를 활용해 사고하고 소통
- **Other Applications**: 논의 없이 발표될 수 있는 다른 주제들에도 적용 가능

---

**오른쪽 패널 (THE CONVERSATION)**

**Opening**
The principal calls all the staff to the staff room just before school for a five-minute announcement.

**Objective Level**
Our school policy is that a parent who has custody of a child may sign a release from allowing someone else to pick up their child from school. Johnny's mother has signed one to allow his uncle to pick him and his sisters up. Johnny has just come crying to school and told me some confidential information.

**Reflective Level**
I am very upset by what I have heard.

**Interpretive Level**
In my analysis of the situation, Johnny's and his sisters' safety may be at stake if they go with their uncle today after school.

**Decisional Level**
No one is to allow Johnny or his sisters to go with his uncle, either during the day, or after school. I want to know immediately if the uncle or anyone comes looking for them today. If there is any question, bring them personally to my office. I will be trying to contact Johnny's mother.

**Closing**
Does everyone understand this? Will you all operate out of what I am asking?
There's the bell. I'll see you later.

---
*Creative Applications 229*

## 페이지 243 (SKU-000671170_11_00243.jpeg)

# 230 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Using the Four Levels as a Format for a Report Form: Simple Team Report

### Situation
When a team is unable to come together for regular progress reports, this "conversation" can be sent out as a form to be filled in — it can even be e-mailed.

**Rational Aim:** To evaluate the work of the past year.

**Experiential Aim:** To share learnings and determine future challenges.

**Hints:** Each of these reports can be sent to everyone else on the team, or they can be compiled into one and sent out...

**Other Applications:** Questions like this can be put on an interactive website or a list serve for the whole group to respond to.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Please use these questions to evaluate the work of the team.

**Objective Questions**
- What have been key results and outcomes of our past work?
- Give some examples as evidence of these key results and outcomes.

**Reflective Questions**
- What's worked?
- What did not work?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What are some important learnings from what we have done?
- What are some challenges facing us?

**Decisional Questions**
- What implications do you see for this year, and beyond this year?
- What will it take to overcome these challenges?

**Closing**
Please return your answers as soon as possible so they can be collated with those from other members of the team.

---

## 페이지 244 (SKU-000671170_11_00244.jpeg)

# Focused Conversation Embedded in an Icebreaker: Team-building Process

## Situation
A school team in Arizona does an exercise to get to know each other at the beginning of the year. The exercise starts with a video on teamwork. Then each person is given a page with a drawing of a compass with lines to put a person's name at each of the four points of North, South, East and West.

*[나침반 그림]*

**Rational Aim**
To process a video on teamwork.

**Experiential Aim**
To break the ice and meet a number of new people.

**Hints**
You may want to put the four steps of the message on a chart.
The worksheet is complex, but it provides a tool for making sure people talk to more than one person.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
Let's use this drawing of a compass with others' names to mix us up and process our learnings from the video. Each person finds four people that they don't know well, and each puts their name at one of the corners of the compass for the other.

### Objective Questions
*(NORTH Partner = WHAT or FACTS — Discuss facts only here, not feeling.)*
Find your NORTH partner (the person whose name is on your compass at the North point), then look at me please. With your NORTH partner, discuss WHAT you remember from the video.
Discuss FACTS:
- What words do you remember?
- What pictures can you recall?

*(Give 1-2 minutes for partner discussion, then pull group back together with signal — hand raised or other signal. Ask for a few volunteers to share some facts with the group.)*

### Reflective Questions
*(SOUTH partner = GUT or REACTIONS)*
Thank your NORTH partner and find your SOUTH partner, then look at me please.
With your SOUTH partner, discuss the GUT or REACTIONS you had watching the video.
- How did you feel during the video?
- Where were your feelings most uplifted? Most anxious? Most challenged?

*(Give 1-2 minutes for partner discussion, then pull group back together with signal — hand raised or other signal. Ask for a few volunteers to share some reactions with the group.)*

### Interpretive Questions
*(EAST partner = SO WHAT, or IMPLICATIONS)*
Thank your SOUTH partner, find your EAST partner, then look at me please *(wait).*
We've shared WHAT or facts and GUT or REACTIONS. Now we'll discuss a bit more deeply the SO WHAT, or IMPLICATIONS.
What are the implications of what we just viewed for our school?

*(continued)*

---
*Creative Applications 231*

---

## 페이지 245 (SKU-000671170_11_00245.jpeg)

## 232 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

### Focused Conversation Embedded in an Icebreaker: Team-building Process *(continued)*

How are we as a team, often similar to what we just viewed?
*(Discuss in pairs — volunteers then share with group.)*

**Decisional Questions**
(WEST partner = NOW WHAT or ACTIONS)
Thank your EAST partner. Now find your WEST partner. Look at me please.
We've shared WHAT or facts, GUT or reactions, SO WHAT or implications:
Now we'll focus on NOW WHAT or actions.
What actions do we need to take to foster teamwork?
What steps can we take to support teamwork?
*(Discuss in pairs — volunteers then share with group.)*

**Closing**
Thank your WEST partner and return to your original seat.
The dialogue technique we've just used is called the Focused Conversation Method.
Four parts are necessary for rich, meaningful discussion:
- O ...objective or FACTS ........................WHAT
- R ...reflective or REACTIONS .............GUT
- I ...interpretive or IMPLICATIONS ...SO WHAT
- D ...decisional or ACTIONS.................NOW WHAT

---

## 페이지 246 (SKU-000671170_11_00246.jpeg)

# Using the Four-Level Process on an Evaluation Form: Strategic Planning Process Evaluation and Feedback Form

## 좌측 컬럼

**Situation**
A facilitator has just led a school in a participatory strategic planning process. He hands out a quick feedback form with questions and spaces to write answers.

**Rational Aim**
To have solid, thought-through feedback on the process.

**Experiential Aim**
To enable participants to experience their wisdom and journey affirmed.

**Hints**
This makes a good generic evaluation form for training and participatory events. Be sure to leave enough room for writing answers.

**Other Applications**
For a training event, the last questions can be "How will you apply the process?" and "What further training are you interested in?"
This can also be held as a conversation to wrap up a day.

---

## 우측 컬럼: THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Could you please take a minute to fill out this form before you leave the room?

**Objective Questions**
What were two or three key events of this process for you?

**Reflective Questions**
What were high points?
What were low points?

**Interpretive Questions**
What were important accomplishments and/or information?
Please complete this statement in a sentence or two: The significance of this process for me has been....
Rate this process on a scale of 1 to 10, with 10 being the highest. Circle one.

**Decisional Questions**
What suggestions do you have to improve this process?
Looking to the next year or two, what suggestions do you have for how we evaluate and measure the effectiveness of the plans we have decided on?

**Closing**
Thank you. Please leave on the table for the facilitator to pick up.

---
*Creative Applications 233*

---

## 페이지 247 (SKU-000671170_11_00247.jpeg)

# 234 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Using the Four-Level Process on a Survey Form: Survey on the Implementation of a New Statewide Initiative

---

### [좌측 컬럼: Situation]

**Situation**
Teachers are being introduced to a new statewide initiative for assessment. They have used the initiative for a year. The following conversation is sent to teachers as a survey to reflect on and return to the administration.

**Rational Aim**
To have data on how the assessment initiative is working in the individual classroom.

**Experiential Aim**
To have a sense of being valued and heard.

**Other Applications**
Although this is written as a survey to be filled out by individuals, the same questions could be used in focus groups or in school staff conversations, or with parent groups.

---

### [우측 컬럼: THE CONVERSATION]

**Opening**
This survey is on the implementation of the assessment initiative. Please take twenty minutes to go through these questions and give your honest responses. We will use your thoughts to improve the initiative.

**Objective Questions**
- What assessment activities have you done in your class in the past year?
- What interventions have you done in your class in the past year?

**Reflective Questions**
- As you have conducted assessment and interventions in your class what has surprised you? What worried you?
- What pleased you?

**Interpretive Questions**
- How has your use of the assessment and intervention initiative affected the ability of your students to achieve the state standards in your class?
- What are the weaknesses of the assessment and intervention initiative in your grade level?
- What are its strengths?

**Decisional Questions**
- What are your next steps in using the assessment and intervention strategies in your class?
- What recommendations would you make to administration, based on your experience?

**Closing**
Please return this survey to administration.

---

## 페이지 252 (SKU-000671170_11_00252.jpeg)

# Solution Focused Personal Goal Setting on Professional Accountability for School Leadership Teams

---

## 좌측 사이드바

**Designed for**
Students – Elementary

**Situation**
A school leadership team is exploring the application of professional accountability based on personal experience, professional readings and dialogue. Pre-meeting readings have been sent out with instructions to make margin notations: * for stand out ideas; ? for questions, uncertainties; Ö for agreements.

**Rational Aim**
To engage members of the leadership team by acknowledging their background knowledge and support capacity building as it relates to accountability.

**Experiential Aim**
Through personal reflection and collegial dialogue, to encourage ownership and modeling of professional accountability in support of the development of shared leadership and professional learning community among all staff.

**Concrete Beginning Point:**
Readings on professional accountability, sent out before the meeting.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening

- 사전 독서 자료와 여백 표기 지참 필요: `*` 두드러진 아이디어, `?` 질문/불확실성, `Ö` 동의

- 플레이스매트 중앙 박스에 개별 작성:
  *By the end of this meeting on professional accountability what do I hope to know, be, have?*

- 척도 질문 (1–10):
  > 1 ————————————— 10

### Objective Questions
- What do I already know about professional accountability?
- What are the key ideas from the readings?

### Reflective Questions
- Which of these ideas stood out for me (starred items) and why?
- Which of these ideas did I agree with (checked items) and why?
- Which of these ideas left me with questions or uncertainty (questioned items) and why?

### Interpretive Questions
*(As a large group)*
- So how did this article enhance my/our understanding of what it means to be professionally accountable?
- So what might be the significance of these ideas my/our application of professional accountability?
- *Personally:* So how has our conversation assisted me in realizing my goal for this meeting?

---
*Additional Conversations from Second Edition* — p. 239

## 페이지 253 (SKU-000671170_11_00253.jpeg)

# 240 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Educational Quality (EQAO) results for the Grade Nine Assessment of Mathematics

---

### Situation

A school has received their student results from EQAO (Educational Quality Assessment of Ontario). For the third year in a row, the student results have gone down. The administration asks for a facilitator to work with the math department to try and determine how to address the issue of lower marks on a province wide test.

**Rational Aim**
To identify priorities for improvement on the Grade 9 Assessment of Mathematics

**Experiential Aim**
To develop and promote the ability to work collaboratively to improve student learning.

**Concrete Beginning Point:**
Detailed School Results for the latest Grade 9 Assessment of Mathematics

**Hints:**
It is very important to record the responses at the Decisional level. They can be used again to revisit the topic.

**Other Applications:**
This conversation can be used with any testing or performance data at any level.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

#### Opening

Here is the report for the Detailed School Results for the latest Grade 9 Assessment of Mathematics. We will take a short time to skim through the data. I will ask some questions. We will focus on facts first, then connections and responses, then interpretation and finally implications for action. The report is divided into several categories; contextual data, gender data, English as a Second Language and Special Education data and results over time. We will look at each section separately first, then think about the overall report.

#### Objective Questions

What data catches your eye (in each of the categories)?
What is unclear to you?
What ranking does the report give our students compared with the board and the province?
*(Repeat these three questions for each category. This can be done as a jigsaw activity.)*

#### Reflective Questions

What surprises you in this information?
What most concerns you?
How does this data compare with your intuitive or personal experience of students' achievement?

#### Interpretive Questions

What are our students' areas of strength or weakness?
What may be some of the underlying causes?
What are some emerging themes in all of this information?

#### Decisional Questions

In order to build on our strengths and deal with weaknesses, what areas are the highest priority for improvement in our department?
*(Record on chart paper)*
What are two or three things that we could focus on immediately?
*(Record on chart paper)*
Who will work on the plans and the actions for each priority?
*(Record on chart paper)*

#### Closing

This is tremendous work and it will make a difference in our students' performance. Thank you for your input and participation today.

---

# Book Report

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition* 241

---

**Book Report**

| Field | |
|---|---|
| **Report by** | _______________ |
| **on** *(name of book)* | _______________ |
| **by** *(author of book)* | _______________ |

---

Who were the main characters in this story? What happened in this story?

What is your reaction to this story? What parts of this story did you like? What did you not like?

What character in the story is most like you?

Where have you experienced something like this? Describe your experience.

What was this story really about? What can it tell you about your own life?

What have you learned from this story?

What will you do differently as a result of what you have learned?

## 페이지 255 (SKU-000671170_11_00255.jpeg)

# 242 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Analyzing Report Card Comments

### Situation
A group of teachers have come to participate in an in-service on writing good comments

**Rational Aim**
To identify aspects of very good report card comments

**Experiential Aim**
To build confidence in writing good comments

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Samples of report card comments

**Hints**
Get him clearly in your mind, and have a sense of what his/her marks will be. Think now about his/her parents. You are the expert on this student, having seen his/her work in a variety of circumstances and situations.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**

Working Assumptions
- Everyone has wisdom
- We need everyone's wisdom to get the wisest result.
- There are no wrong answers.
- The whole is greater than the sum of its parts.
- Everyone will hear others and be heard.

We have some sample report card comments in front of us. Let's take a few minutes to look at ones that other teachers and parents have found helpful to see what we can learn from them about writing good comments. Then we'll do an exercise to apply what we've learned.

**Objective Questions**
- What do you notice about these report card comments?
- What strikes you about these report card comments?
- What commonalities do you observe?

**Reflective Questions**
- What is the best comment you see?
- What comment confuses you or makes you wonder?
- What comment do you think reflects the student well?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What principles can we see in good report card comments from these?
- What is missing in these report card comments?
- What makes good report card comments?
- What do the parents of your students want to know about their children?

**Decisional Questions**
- What do you want to include in your report card comments?
- How will your report card comments reflect your students?

**Closing**
This exercise in looking at good comments made by others allows us to move next to writing report card comments for your students. I would like you now to think of the student who be the hardest to write comments for.

---

## 페이지 256 (SKU-000671170_11_00256.jpeg)

# Understanding Differences between Assessment *for* Learning and Assessment *of* Learning

## 좌측 패널

**Situation**
An elementary school staff is beginning to focus on assessment for learning as a school. To begin their focus they are exploring the differences between assessment for learning (AFL) and assessment of learning (AOL).

**Rational Aim**
Staff will understand the differences between AFL & AOL.

**Experiential Aim**
The group will start to recognize how assessment for learning will benefit their students.

**Concrete Beginning Point:**
Document describing two kinds of assessments

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
The staff are given a document that clearly articulates the different aspects of both AFL & AOL from their local assessment consortia. They read through the document together.

### Objective Questions
- What does the document say assessment for learning is?
- What does the document say assessment of learning is?

### Reflective Questions
- What gets your attention here?
- What surprises you?
- Give an example of where you've seen either of these kinds of assessment in real life.

### Interpretive Questions
- What is a key insight you had as you read this?
- What does this indicate or tell you?
- What are you discovering?
- What impact does each type of assessment have on students?

### Decisional Questions
- What is the first action you as a staff need to take?
- What areas will you need to focus on?

### Closing
We have taken our first step on our assessment journey by identifying the differences between AFL & AOL, and we have identified a few next steps. The potential for our students is exciting and I look forward to the rest of the journey.

---
*Additional Conversations from Second Edition* **243**

## 페이지 257 (SKU-000671170_11_00257.jpeg)

# Assessment Strategies

**244 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS**

---

## 좌측 정보 패널

| 항목 | 내용 |
|------|------|
| **Designed for** | Students – Elementary |
| **Situation** | A group of ECS teachers across the district have come together in a division-wide PD day to share assessments. |
| **Rational Aim** | To identify effective assessment strategies across the district at the Kindergarten level. |
| **Experiential Aim** | Each person will experience that they have insight, and respect others' insights |
| **Concrete Beginning Point** | Sample assessment strategies shared by each person |
| **Hints** | Each participant needs to come prepared with several examples of assessment strategies. |

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
Look at the variety of sample assessments the group has brought in. Each person shares an assessment strategy with the rest of the group.

Describe it succinctly.

### Objective Questions
*(After each is shared)* What questions of clarification do you have?

### Reflective Questions
Which aspects of evaluation and assessment do you find most difficult or most frustrating?

Which aspects do you find most helpful, useful or successful?

### Interpretive Questions
What do you see that "works" or really shows promise?

What are some of the differences among the assessments?

What aspects of the assessment strategies make them effective?

### Decisional Questions
What have you learned this afternoon that you will be able to use in your classroom?

### Closing
Collectively this group has a lot of expertise and wisdom. Opportunities like this allow us all an opportunity to benefit from that expertise.

## 페이지 258 (SKU-000671170_11_00258.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition 245

## Book Study – School Teams

### 왼쪽 컬럼 (설계 정보)

**Designed for**
Students – Elementary

**Situation**
A Professional Learning Community group is doing a series of study sessions to keep on top of current educational literature, particularly to be able to guide school teams.

**Rational Aim**
Understand what makes a school team effective

**Experiential Aim**
Commitment to apply learnings from the paper

**Concrete Beginning Point:**
Paper, "How Can We Help Teams Focus on the Issues That Impact Student Learning?", part of a chapter on "Building the Collaborative Culture of a Professional Learning Community", from Ch. 5 *Learning by Doing*, written by Dufour, Dufour, Eaker and Many, Solution Tree, July 1, 2006.)

**Hints**
In the interpretive level, you may need to push a bit for participants to name concrete examples. It is important to ground theory in real experience to see its relevance and to be committed to using it.

**Other Applications**
Change the intent and the interpretive questions, and use it to study any paper.

---

### 오른쪽 컬럼 (THE CONVERSATION)

**Opening**

**Objective Questions**
What words or phrases stand out for you? *(paragraph by paragraph)*

**Reflective Questions**
What in this paper strikes you as really familiar?
What do you find intriguing?

**Interpretive Questions**
What are some examples of where you've seen a team (in the way they describe it) in real life?
What does this kind of collaboration look like in real life? Give some examples.
Which of the definitions or suggestions in this paper would have a positive impact on the teams you work with?

**Decisional Questions**
What is a practical step you can take in real life to apply what you've learned from this conversation?

**Closing**
As we've talked about this paper, we have added a lot to its content. I can see how we can apply it effectively.

---

## 페이지 259 (SKU-000671170_11_00259.jpeg)

# Understanding Data to Build School Goals for the Fall

*(Page 246 - THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS)*

---

## Left Column

**Situation**
An elementary school team is looking at data to build school goals to improve student achievement in the next year.

**Rational Aim**
A consensus on curriculum aspects for focussed improvement in the fall at each level.

**Experiential Aim**
Feel progress and clarity about fall direction

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Printed student achievement data

**Hints**
Data doesn't tell the whole story, and it is easy to find loopholes in it that allow people to escape responsibility for changing the way they teach. Take time in the interpretive level to explore the areas of improvement needed. You could add the question "What might be some specific reasons (within our control or ability to affect) that students are not achieving?"

---

## Right Column: THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**

We need to understand a wide variety of data, and come to a consensus on what piece of the whole picture we want to focus on for improving students' achievement in the fall.

We have the afternoon to work on this. I hope to move you through the first part in about an hour or a little more so you have some work time to make personal and specific plans that carry out this focus.

**Objective Questions**

- Let's look through your data on student achievement from this year.
- What does the data say that your students have demonstrated that they can do well?
- In what areas have they done less well?
- How do boys and girls compare in their achievement scores?

**Reflective Questions**

- Now let's move to thinking about what the data means to each of us personally.
- What makes you proud about this data?
- What makes you uncomfortable or concerned about this data?

**Interpretive Questions**

- Which areas are strong and we need to just keep doing what we're doing?
- In which areas do we need to improve student achievement?
- What are some ways that we can affect student achievement in the areas we've identified?

**Decisional Questions**

- Which of these things can we all commit to doing?
- Who will take responsibility for the next step?
- What is the responsibility of each person?

**Closing**

Thank you to each of your for working with me to use this methodology — I hope it's been helpful to you in working through what you want and need to do for the fall.

---

## 페이지 260 (SKU-000671170_11_00260.jpeg)

# Peer Coaching Conversation to Enhance Professional Learning and Practice

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 247*

---

## 표/도해 요약

**왼쪽 사이드바:**
- **Situation:** 두 교사가 협력하여 효과적인 수업을 반성하고 계획함
- **Rational Aim:** 의미 있는 반성과 효과적인 계획을 위한 코칭 기술 연습
- **Experiential Aim:** 코칭 교사의 역량, 장인정신, 협업 강화; 바꾸어 말하기, 대기 시간, 질문 기술 적용
- **Concrete Beginning Point:** 전날 수업
- **Hints:** 코칭 대화에서 바꾸어 말하기와 대기 시간은 관계 형성과 의미 있는 반성을 위해 중요함. 질문은 개방형이며 바꾸어 말하기 후에 사용됨

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
We're going to work together so I can practice my coaching skills and you can reflect on and plan your lesson. I won't be giving advice, but instead will help you access what you already know through using the skills of paraphrasing, wait time, and questioning.

### Objective Questions
- Reflecting back on yesterday's lesson: What happened?
- What did you observe?
- What did the students do?
- What did you do?
- What data/evidence did you collect to know if the lesson was effective?

### Reflective Questions
- How do you feel it went? How do you know?
- What data/evidence do you have to support your impressions?

### Interpretive Questions
- What comparisons have you made to other lessons? with this class?
- What conclusions would you draw?
- What do you know now that you didn't know then?
- What adaptions are you considering?

### Decisional Questions
As you begin planning for tomorrow's lesson:
- What is your intention, objective, goal?
- What is uppermost for you to attend to?
- What steps will you take?
- What resources do you need?
- How will you know you are successful?

### Closing
- How has this coaching conversation helped you?
- What feedback do you have for me, the "coach"?
- What might I do differently next time to assist you?

---

## 페이지 261 (SKU-000671170_11_00261.jpeg)

# 248 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Collaborative School Culture

### Situation
A Professional Learning Community group is doing a series of study sessions to keep on top of current educational literature, particularly to create a collaborative school culture.

### Rational Aim
To understand how to increase collegial relations in the school to strengthen professional practice.

### Experiential Aim
Confidence that we're on the right track and commitment to take risks to improve relations.

### Concrete Beginning Point
Paper: "Improving Relations Within the Schoolhouse" by Roland S. Barth, from Educational Leadership, March 2006.

### Hints
The "jigsaw" process at the objective level helps a large group get a sense of a whole article speedily.

The conversation leader needs to be very familiar with the article to be able to keep the group focused and moving.

### Other Applications
Serious editing of the aims and the details of the objective and interpretive levels will make this conversation useful for other papers.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
*(요약)* 학교 내 동료 관계 향상 방법 이해를 위한 대화. 복잡한 논문을 함께 읽고 토론.

### Objective Questions
- 도입부 핵심 단어 / 4개 섹션별 그룹 토론 / 3섹션 및 결론 검토

### Reflective Questions
- "아하!" 순간 / 유사 경험 공유

### Interpretive Questions
- 실행 용이/어려운 제안 / 학교에 가장 큰 영향을 미칠 것

### Decisional Questions
- 학습 요약 / 적용 방법 / 다음 단계

### Closing
학교 내 작은 변화들이 학생 학습에 기여하는 관계에 큰 영향을 미칠 수 있음.

## 페이지 262 (SKU-000671170_11_00262.jpeg)

# Interpreting Results of Community Dialogue Regarding School Organization

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 249*

---

## Situation
The Board of Directors has consulted with the community regarding their consultant's proposal on school organization. They have a report on the community data, and they need to seriously consider the community's views to move forward on school reorganization.

**Rational Aim**
The board will interpret the results of the community dialogue and consider significant themes, and identify criteria to appraise future plans.

**Experiential Aim**
The board will feel pleased with their thoughtful consideration of this issue and confident about their ability to make high-quality decisions on school organization.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Report on Results of Community Dialogue

**Hints**
- Use the flipchart in the interpretive and decisional levels to record answers so that the board has a record of its responses.
- You may want to ask the Superintendent (or Board Chair) for their responses directly if they have been reticent to share their views. These are important perspectives that need to be transparent during the process.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
We're here to review the community views on school organization, consider its significance, and then to identify criteria to appraise future plans and ideas. This work session will utilize a structured process to understand the community data and use it.

Please take five minutes and identify the five items that "grab your attention" in the report.

In pairs, please share your lists.

### Objective Questions
- One person at a time, please tell us one concept or comment that you notice in this report.
- What else "grabbed you?"
- What is not clear to you?

### Reflective Questions
- What do you read in this report that is encouraging?
- What troubles you?

### Interpretive Questions
- What patterns do you notice in the responses?
- What themes?
- What seems to be the most important payoff for students from the perspective of community?
- What worries members of the community the most about this initiative?

### Decisional Questions
- What must the Board take into consideration as it makes future decisions?
- Which of these concerns and criteria should the Board be sure to use in appraising and assessing future plans and actions?
- How will this list be helpful to the Board in moving on this topic?

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 263 (SKU-000671170_11_00263.jpeg)

# 250 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Interpreting Results of Community Dialogue Regarding School Organization *(continued)*

| | **Closing** |
|---|---|
| | What did we do in this process? |
| | What questions did you consider? |
| | In what ways has this session been meaningful? |
| | In what ways was this not meaningful? |
| | How well does the Board understand the thinking of the community? |
| | How has the Board translated the thinking of the community as it prepares for future action? |
| | How well are you prepared to make future decisions and plans on this issue? |
| | *Superintendent's Closing:* Thanks for your hard work. |

## 페이지 264 (SKU-000671170_11_00264.jpeg)

# Continuous Improvement Plan

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 251*

---

## 좌측 컬럼

**Situation**
The Continuous Improvement Plan (CIP) has been developed with input from principals and central office staff due to time constraints. The group of school leaders needs to integrate this year's plan with their work, and make recommendations for how the next year's plan will be created.

**Rational Aim**
To understand how our work fits into the Continuous Improvement Plan (CIP).

**Experiential Aim**
To form a commitment to continuous improvement of our work in harmony with the CIP.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Document of the Continuous Improvement Plan (CIP)

**Hints**
Whenever a plan has been made ahead of time and people are being asked to implement something they have not had a voice in creating, there will be resistance for that reason alone. Be straightforward about why it was done, and acknowledge the skepticism and resistance at the reflective level. Then ask the group what the positive and negative implications are at the interpretive level, and how they can best implement it at the decisional level. This conversation also asks the group how best to get their input into the next plan before it is made.

---

## 우측 컬럼: THE CONVERSATION

### Opening

**Working Assumptions**
- Everyone has wisdom
- We need everyone's wisdom to get the wisest result.
- There are no wrong answers.
- The whole is greater than the sum of its parts.
- Everyone will hear others and be heard.

In planning for the next CIP cycle, let's reflect for a short time on what we understand of the Continuous Improvement Plan, and think about what implications it has for our division and for our own, individual work. The final question will be "What will you do to advance the Strategic Priorities through the Key Actions?"

### Objective Questions
- As you look at the document of the CIP, what stands out for you in the Priority Strategies?
- What Key Actions speak most to your work?
- What does the document say about the process for developing the Continuous Improvement Plan?

### Reflective Questions
- What part of the plan appeals to you the most?
- What part of the plan do you find most distant to your work?
- What parts are you skeptical about?

### Interpretive Questions
- Looking through the CIP, what reading do you get of our school district?
- What might the impact of the CIP be for students in our division?
- Which parts might impact which types of students?
- What parts of the CIP support the work you're doing?
- What parts of the CIP are the most challenging for you/us to implement?

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 265 (SKU-000671170_11_00265.jpeg)

# 252 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Continuous Improvement Plan *(continued)*

---

**Decisional Questions**

What are possible next steps for you and the leadership team in advancing the Key Actions and Strategic Priorities of the CIP?

What can we do to move our next conversation to consider, critically and creatively, the development of the 2007/2008 CIP cycle?

**Closing**

Thank you for your time and thoughtfulness today. This is a major focusing of the work we do in our school division. It is important for everyone to understand it and work towards the improvement of all that we do so that our students, their families and our community benefit.

---

## 페이지 266 (SKU-000671170_11_00266.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition 253

## Preparing for a Debate

### Situation
Students in Grade 7 (Secondary) Social Studies / Humanities Classes are preparing to debate issues in their classroom (selected topics/themes such as the pro and con of conflict – man vs man; man vs nature, etc.). Students are familiar with using an "ORID placemat" to gather information or ideas from readings, notes and class discussions.

**Rational Aim:** Students will demonstrate understanding of curriculum concept(s) and underlying factors that influenced decisions (political issues, governmental structures, etc.) through using the ORID framework to organize information & prepare for their debates.

**Experiential Aim:** Students will develop empathy for others through exploring the emotional factors inherent in a particular role or perspective.

**Concrete Beginning Point:** Research materials such as articles, books, videos, web pages, interview notes.

**Hints:** Students may benefit from working in pairs, to help 'talk out the information, build vocabulary and support understanding of a variety of perspectives.

*(continued)*

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
We will use a placemat to prepare for and research individual topics. Take notes in the appropriate section of the placemat to answer the questions. You can do this with a partner or alone, as you like.

**Objective Questions**
- What facts do you know that pertain to this topic?
- What did you hear, see, or read about incidents surrounding the issue, place or time?

**Reflective Questions**
- How did it feel to live or be in this time or place?
- What were the emotional issues or factors that contributed to the conflict?
- What are some emotions (descriptive words) that you would feel in a similar situation?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What is the significance of the emotional reactions or responses in this situation?
- What will happen if these feelings are not recognized?
- In what ways will these feelings contribute to a final outcome or resolution?

**Decisional Questions**
- Based on this information, what should we do?
- Do you recommend a vote for (pro) or against (con) this argument? Why?

**Closing**
You can use your conclusions and the contributing analysis to present your debate.

---

## 페이지 267 (SKU-000671170_11_00267.jpeg)

# 254 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Preparing for a Debate *(continued)*

---

**Other Applications**

Students can use the placemat format as well to record ideas as participants during actual debate presentations. A similar process may be used for a novel study – having small groups discuss chapters; predict what may happen next; or exploring ramifications of a change in sequence of events to the final outcome etc.

**Name/Comment**

Barbara Milne

Teachers reported that quality of debates, characterized by preparation and organization of arguments both for and against issues, rose dramatically when ORID was used as a framework for organizing the debate as well as debriefing and weighing presenters' arguments". Also, "Students were more engaged in the issues at stake, and less swayed by the 'personality' of presenters".

---

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition — 255

---

## Debriefing Vandalism

### Situation
The staff at the recreation centre are upset about an incident of vandalism that has occurred to a mural that they created in one of the programs.

### Rational Aim
Staff will share their concerns and participate in developing solutions to the issue of vandalism and its effect on the program.

### Experiential Aim
Develop communication and teamwork among the staff through and open ended interactive discussion.

### Concrete Beginning Point
The mural and the the incident of vandalism to it

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Let's have a brief discussion about the vandalism that happened to our mural.

**Objective Questions**
- What happened to the mural?
- What did you see and hear about this incident?

**Reflective Questions**
- What upset you the most when you saw the mural?
- What other reactions did you have?
- What was the reaction of your participants?
- What do you remember thinking about the situation?
- What are your gut responses to this situation?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What effect does a situation like this have on staff and participants?
- What do the reactions to this vandalism tell you about your work with youth?
- What are some possible reasons for this happening?
- What are some things we can do to address these reasons?

**Decisional Questions**
- What steps do we need to take action?
- Who must be involved in this process?
- How can we involve your participants in addressing this situation?
- What should we do next?

**Closing**
Thank you for participating in this discussion. Your efforts have shown me that you are passionate about the work that you do and the participants that you mentor.

---

## 페이지 269 (SKU-000671170_11_00269.jpeg)

# 256 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Debriefing Youth Event

### Situation
Youth staff at the recreation centre has just finished a major event. You lead the group in a debriefing of the event to get opinion on the quality of the event.

**Rational Aim**
Get staff feedback on the about the event and understand the importance of evaluations in the planning process.

**Experiential Aim**
Have staff experience open-ended group process communication that brings closure to their work.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Shared experience of the event

**Hints**
Use an image like "video" at the objective level to help people stay with observations of what was going on rather than subjectivity at the objective level. Each person will have seen things that others didn't see.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
We have just finished a great event for youth in this community. Let's talk about our experience putting on this event.

**Objective Questions**
Imagine you are looking at a video of this event. What are some of the things that happened?
What did you see or hear from participants in this event?

**Reflective Questions**
What parts of this event stand out for you about this event?
What were the high/low points of this event?
How did you feel when you were participating in the event?
What things worked well?

**Interpretive Questions**
What does your participation in this event tell you about yourself?
What does it tell you about your staff team?
What recommendations would you make about this event?

**Decisional Questions**
What things should we do differently next time, having gone through this event?
What do we need to do to implement these recommendations?

**Closing**
Thank you for your thoughts. With your feedback we can continue to improve our teamwork and the quality of programs we create for the youth in this community.

# Department SMART Goals

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 257*

---

## 표 구조 요약

**[왼쪽 열: 상황 설명]**

- **Situation:** A high school department must make SMART goals that are aligned with the overall school goal. They have very little time.
- **Rational Aim:** Department will decide on a S.M.A.R.T. goal that is aligned with the overall school goal.
- **Experiential Aim:** Department members will be collectively focused on a goal, and committed to taking action towards achieving that goal.
- **Concrete Beginning Point:** Overall School Goal, Achievement Data printed so all can see.

---

**[오른쪽 열: THE CONVERSATION]**

### Opening
1. Designate timekeeper.
2. Designate minute-recorder
3. Share rational aim.
4. Participants agree on norms for the collaboration.
5. Set timeline for work for focused conversation

Let's look at our school achievement data and our overall school goal for just a few minutes.

### Objective Questions
- As you look at this, what pops out of the data?
- What do you see happening with student achievement – give a concrete example of the change in a student's achievement?

### Reflective Questions
- What does this look like in your own classroom?

### Interpretive Questions
- What should we celebrate and/or be concerned about?
- What is our department's greatest area of need?

### Decisional Questions
- What components should be included when we create our SMART goal?
- How shall we pull this together into a goal?

### Closing
1. Have someone read through the final decisions.
2. Final comments and opinions

# 258 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Designing Computer Centre Youth Program

### Situation
At the recreation centre the director approaches a group of youth for their input on a March Break Youth Program for a new Computer Centre.

**Rational Aim**
To understand what ideas and activities will attract youth to a computer centre.

**Experiential Aim**
Each youth consulted will experience a feeling of ownership and responsibility towards the programs developed for the computer centre.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Previous experience with computers

**Hints**
Keep the conversation moving fast with active young people. But make sure quiet ones are heard – make the group wait for their responses, if necessary.

**Other Applications**
Any program for which youth engagement will enhance its relevance, and thus the commitment and participation in the program.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
I want to talk to you today about the new computer centre. We want to create new activities programs that will attract and involve youth to our centre. Let's talk about ideas that you think will work.

**Objective Questions**
What computer activities have you been involved in?

**Reflective Questions**
What is the best experience you've had with computers?
What activities would you like to see happening in a computer program that you attend?
What events do you see happening that would interest you in participating?

**Interpretive Questions**
What would attract youth to a computer centre?
What are the most important qualities of this program?
Why would youth be attracted to this program?
What would youth learn or experience from this program?

**Decisional Questions**
What are the steps we need to take to make this program happen?
What role would you like to take in developing this program?

**Closing**
These are some great ideas. I think we can begin to make these things happen. I hope you will be interested in making this program work for everyone.

## 페이지 272 (SKU-000671170_11_00272.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition — 259

---

## Community Dialogue on School Organization

### Situation
A consultant has made a proposal on school organization for the board. The board would like parents, students, community members, and staff members to give them some feedback on the proposal.

### Rational Aim
A consultant has made a proposal on school organization for the board. The board would like parents, students, community members, and staff members to give them some feedback on the proposal.

### Experiential Aim
The group will be appreciative of the complexity of the issue and reassured that they have been heard.

### Concrete Beginning Point
PowerPoint presentation of proposal for school reorganization.

### Hints
Collect the recommendations on easel sheets, one per question, perhaps leaving room for 7 items with 5 bullets already in place. For a large group, you can put sheets up around the room with a question at the top, then have people walk around and answer the questions on each sheet. If there are too many recommendations in the answers to the first decisional question, you may need to do a "priorities conversation" (an additional quick ORID conversation on the list) to narrow down the final recommendations.

*(continued)*

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
We're here to review information about school organization and provide input. Let's go around the group with each person giving their name and briefly relating their role in our school district. *(Show the PowerPoint presentation.)*

**Objective Questions**
- What jargon or terms were used that it would be helpful to clarify?
- What key points does the proposal make?

**Reflective Questions**
- What excites you about this proposal?
- What concerns you about this proposal?
- What parts of this proposal do you find intriguing?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What seems really important to you?
- What are the implications for students?
- What are the implications for parents?
- What are the implications for teachers?
- How does this school organization affect local communities in the district?
- How does this proposal affect the entire district?
- Let's take a look at what we are saying *(Read each list aloud.)*
- What patterns do you see here?

**Decisional Questions**
- Given these implications, what are some things you would like the board to consider?
- How would you summarize our consensus in 2-3 recommendations or considerations we, the whole group, want to identify for the school board?

**Closing**
Thank you for your thoughtful input. This work will be collected and compiled with the work of other groups and presented to the school board.

*(continued)*

---

## Community Dialogue on School Organization *(continued)*

| 좌측 설명 | 우측 질문 목록 |
|---|---|
| The reflection in the closing allows the group to process a difficult meeting before they leave, which helps support the decisions reached in the meeting. | *Quick reflection to process the experience of the meeting:* |

**Quick reflection to process the experience of the meeting:**

- What did we do?
- What words or phrases were used?
- In what ways was this session meaningful for you?
- What was not meaningful?
- How has your appreciation of the issue changed?
- What would you tell someone who was not here when she asked, "What did you do?"
- Thanks again for your hard work.
