## 페이지 274 (SKU-000671170_11_00274.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition 261

---

## Using the Data Wall to Evaluate School Achievement

### Situation
The province expects school improvement related to achievement on quality assessment. School staff are to evaluate the significance of these and other assessment results, prioritize effective strategies to improve school performance, and act on those strategies.

**Rational Aim**
To identify priorities for improvement in student learning.

**Experiential Aim**
To engender commitment to using a data wall as a tool for improvement.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Student Achievement Data Wall

**Hints**
- A "jigsaw" method may be used where small groups focus on certain sections of the data using the O level questions, then share observations.
- At the I and D levels, write the answers on a flipchart so that the information is available to the group for the next questions.
- In this conversation there will be a tendency to want to answer R and I questions as soon as they see the Data Wall. This may lead to defensiveness rather than thoughtful evaluation.

*(continued)*

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**

Here is our school Data Wall which includes our quality (EQAO) results and student achievement data from: standardized testing; DRA, PM Benchmark, or CASI assessment; report card data; and board and provincial EQAO results.

Let's take a short time to skim through the data, and then I am going to ask the questions I have posted on the flip chart. We will focus on facts first, then connections, then interpretation, and finally implications for action.

**Objective Questions**
- What data catches your eye in each of the categories?
- What facts stand out?
- What questions of clarity do you have?
- What is unclear to you?

**Reflective Questions**
- What surprises you in this information?
- What most concerns you?
- How does this data compare with your intuitive or personal experience of students' achievements?

**Interpretive Questions**
- Where are we strong relative to expectations?
- Where are we weak relative to expectations?
- What may be some of the underlying causes?
- What are some emerging themes in all this information?
- Which of these is most important for you? Why?
- Which of these needs to be dealt with first? Why?

**Decisional Questions**
- From the standpoint of building on our strengths and dealing with concerns, what areas of skill do you hear the group saying are the highest priorities for improvement in our school?
- Which do you hear the group saying are the lowest priorities at this time?

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 275 (SKU-000671170_11_00275.jpeg)

# 262 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Using the Data Wall to Evaluate School Achievement *(continued)*

| 왼쪽 열 | 오른쪽 열 |
|--------|--------|
| **진행 참고사항** | **토론 질문 및 마무리** |

**[왼쪽 열 내용]**

Watch the flow of answers very carefully. The very first time someone answers a question that has not been asked yet, ask them to hold that response until the question where it will be most appropriate. If you have written the questions down as an agenda, it will be easier. Nipping the tendency to jump ahead in the bud is important in this conversation.

**Other Applications**

With some "tweaking" this could be used to present quality results to groups such as the School Council or Student Council.

---

**[오른쪽 열 내용]**

What three or four of these high priority areas do we most need to focus on improving in the next few years?

Who will work on the plans (and the actions) for each priority?

**Closing**

This is tremendous work, and will make a difference in our students' performance. We will take a couple of weeks for each group to complete an action plan, and then have another quick meeting (date and time) to share the plans.

---

## 페이지 276 (SKU-000671170_11_00276.jpeg)

# Examination of School Data and/or External Data

## 상황 및 구성 정보

| 항목 | 내용 |
|------|------|
| **Situation** | Joint middle-school (feeder) and secondary school principals examining school data to determine next steps |
| **Rational Aim** | All participants will leave with a concrete next step based on the dialogue about the data |
| **Experiential Aim** | All participants will feel more comfortable about examining data |
| **Concrete Beginning Point** | Pages of collected student data |
| **Hints** | School data is potentially explosive and can lead to defensive postures or surface strong emotions. Data must be contextualized and shared with anyone who has a stake in its use |
| **Other Applications** | Use with a whole staff or a department |

---

## THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**

I'm going to invite you to examine some data that we've collected for your schools...

**Objective Questions**

What about the data set pops out or catches your eye?

**Reflective Questions**

What about the data encourages you? What about the data concerns you?

**Interpretive Questions**

What patterns or trends among the data do you see emerging?

**Decisional Questions**

What are some concrete next steps we (middle and secondary school principals) can take in terms of using this data in our respective school settings?

**Closing**

Thank you for engaging in a conversation and process that allowed us to interpret and make sense of the data.

---
*Additional Conversations from Second Edition — p. 263*

---

## 페이지 277 (SKU-000671170_11_00277.jpeg)

# 264 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## First Nations and Métis Education Goal Setting

---

### Situation
Each Regina Board of Education school must develop a First Nations and Métis Education Goal for the 2007-08 school year.

**Rational Aim**
To establish a point of reference through reflection for the committee brainstorm a First Nations and Métis Education School Goal.

**Experiential Aim**
To be confident that goals are based in reality and necessity

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Video *For Angela*, 21min., National Film Board, 1993, starring Tina Keeper

**Hints**
This can be followed by one or more consensus workshops to create practical plans for reaching the broad goal. The decisional level question may be restated as the focus question for a consensus workshop: e.g. "What might we do to enhance learning of First Nations and Métis students at Cochrane with this goal in mind?" or "What might we do to enhance learning of non-First Nations and Métis students about First Nation and Métis culture?"

**Other Applications**
This conversation is a good example of how to start with an outside point of reference to spark an insightful conversation about important changes in a situation.

*(continued)*

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**

Each Regina Board of Education school must develop a First Nations and Métis Education Goal for the 2007-08 school year. The job of this committee is to develop a school goal for Cochrane for 2007-08.

Participant guidelines:
1. Everyone has wisdom
2. We need everyone's wisdom for the wisest result
3. There are no wrong answers
4. The whole is greater than the sum of its parts
5. Everyone will hear others and be heard

*(View video.)*

---

**Objective Questions**

- Who are the characters in the video story?
- Where did the story take place?
- What caught your attention in the video?
- What lines of the dialogue do you recall?

**Reflective Questions**

- Where did you feel "warm" or "good" in the story?
- Where did you witness people's hope or excitement?
- Where did you find yourself in the story?
- With whom did you first identify?
- What does this story remind you of, or what memories or associations were triggered in you as you viewed the video story?

**Interpretive Questions**

- What might the insight behind this video story be?
- What clues might it give us about First Nations and Métis students in our school?
- What might we learn from this about how we address the learning of First Nations and Métis students?

*(continued)*

---

We came away from the focused conversation charged with hope and satisfaction in what we accomplished as a group." | **Closing** Thank you very much. |

## 페이지 279 (SKU-000671170_11_00279.jpeg)

# Grade 9 Math Task Analysis

## Situation
The math consultant is working with a cross-panel group of grade 6-9 teachers to plan how to support students to be successful in grade 9 math. They decide to start with the learning artefacts – the math tasks that students will encounter throughout the course. They provide evidence of the concept knowledge, skills, the student performances and the mathematical thinking that is valued in grade 9 mathematics. They have already done a brainstorm of Grade 9 math tasks. This conversation is to analyze the implications for grades 6-9 classrooms.

**Rational Aim:** To develop shared knowledge and understanding of what students are learning and be in a position to consider the implications of this information for our classroom practice across grades 6 to 9.

**Experiential Aim:** To share in the urgency to support successful transitions from middle school to high school through mathematics.

**Concrete Beginning Point:** Previously brainstormed list of Grade 9 math tasks

**Other Applications:** This conversation could be done with any subject for which there are clear tasks.

*(continued)*

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
*(summarized: Introduces the purpose of using math tasks as learning artefacts to build cross-panel understanding of Grade 9 expectations across grades 6–9.)*

### Objective Questions
- What stands out for you as you review our brainstormed ideas about these grade 9 *(insert strand name)* tasks? What are the main points in our task analysis?

### Reflective Questions
- In what ways does our analysis of the tasks align with your thinking?
- In what ways does our analysis of these tasks raise concerns for you?
- Where will students in our family of schools struggle?
- Where will our students in our family of schools experience success?

### Interpretive Questions
- What are some things that you have learned that will influence: -what you teach? -what you assess?
- What are some things that you have learned that will influence your instructional practices?
- What is most significant for you?

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 280 (SKU-000671170_11_00280.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition 267

## Grade 9 Math Task Analysis *(continued)*

| **Name/Comment** | **Decisional Questions** |
|---|---|
| Cathy Dunne | What do we need to do in our classrooms to provide the necessary experiences for students to be successful in these grade 9 tasks? |
| Both conversations generated the desired results. Teachers worked collaboratively and truly developed a cross panel understanding of the grade 6 to 9 curriculum as a continuum of learning. | **Closing** You have identified some critical areas that you will be focussing on in your classroom practice that will support students to be successful in grade 9. You have also begun exploring how this information will influence what and how you teach in your grade and across grade 6 to 9. Thank you for sharing your insights and commitment to support student success through mathematics |

## 페이지 281 (SKU-000671170_11_00281.jpeg)

# 268 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## High School Renewal

### Situation
A school division is consulting all of its stakeholders to create a school renewal plan. They have a 1-hour window for each focus group. This conversation sets the context for the brainstorm part of a Consensus Workshop that follows. Representatives from each focus group will later gather to complete the workshop process.

**Rational Aim**
To collect thoughtful ideas for directions for high school renewal, to be clustered together later to create a plan for high school renewal

**Experiential Aim**
To experience having a voice in future plans for high schools at the outset of the process, and respect for a diversity of perspectives.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Shared observations of youth behaviour and characteristics of the world around them

**Hints**
The process and sub-questions can be written out on a worksheet handout to guide small groups and individuals in their thinking and recording of ideas. This can speed up the process, especially with large groups.

**Other Applications**
The decisional question becomes the focus question for the Consensus Workshop which follows this initial 15-20 minute conversation. In this situation, the time was limited and only the brainstorm section of the workshop was

*(continued)*

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**

**1) Working Assumptions**
- Everyone has wisdom
- We need everyone's wisdom to get the wisest result.
- There are no wrong answers.
- The whole is greater than the sum of its parts.
- Everyone will hear others and be heard.

**2) Context/Background**

Our school division began a process of consultation with its staff and community one year ago about the renewal of our schools. The School Board would now like to continue this consultation more deeply and widely. A consulting firm has been engaged to design and manage the consultation process.

The first part of the Renewal Consultation will involve high schools this spring, beginning with today's meeting. A high school student forum and an evening forum for parents and community members are being held to gain their input. Focus group facilitators will also meet with Grade 8 students and various groups of high school students participating in our special programs. The Elders' Council will be consulted and community groups will also be invited to provide input.

While the consultation process will begin with high schools this spring, it is intended that a broad spectrum of input will be invited for elementary schools as well. This process will continue after elections in the fall and throughout the next school year. You will be hearing more about the consultation process in the months to come.

Today we begin with your ideas about making high schools more effective in educating our students in the next five to ten years. We will use a quick Focused Conversation in small groups to explore your thinking, and then do some brainstorming to gather ideas from staff in all our high schools. The ideas will be recorded on cards along with any explanations required. A working group of two teachers from each high school (mostly Learning Leaders) will meet in about a month to cluster the pool of ideas into groupings that honour all the input you contribute today. This input will help to provide direction for high schools to take in the next five to ten years. We thank you in advance for your contributions today.

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 282 (SKU-000671170_11_00282.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition 269

## High School Renewal *(continued)*

**[왼쪽 사이드바]**
Art of Focused Conversation for Schools 및 The Workshop Book (Canadian Institute of Cultural Affairs 출판) 참조 안내

---

### Objective Questions
- 지난 10년간 학생들과 세상에서 관찰한 변화
- 학생들이 묻는 질문의 종류
- 학생들의 관심사
- 학생들이 가진 기회의 종류
- 학생들의 세계에서 일어나는 일
- 현재 고등학교에서 잘 작동하는 것

### Reflective Questions
- 젊은이들과 그들의 세계에 대한 우려
- 젊은이들과 그들의 세계에서 흥미로운 것

### Interpretive Questions
- 변화하는 상황이 고등학교에 미치는 시사점
- 고등학교의 기회와 위협
- 학생들이 고등학교에서 더/다르게 필요로 하는 것
- 현재 잘 서비스되는/그렇지 않은 학생 그룹
- 학생 필요를 더 잘 충족하기 위한 방안
- 학생 필요 충족에 도전이 될 것들

### Decisional Questions
향후 5~10년간 학생들이 효과적으로 배우기 위한 고등학교의 모습:
- Organization and leadership
- School climate and culture
- Curriculum and content
- Ways of learning and teaching
- Reaching out to families and community

### Closing
오늘 한 일, 놀랍거나 흥미롭거나 좌절스러운 것, 배운 것, 배운 것의 활용 방안 및 감사 인사

## 페이지 283 (SKU-000671170_11_00283.jpeg)

# 270 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Applying Instructional Intelligence to Our Courses

### Situation
A high school department team is at the end of a session of in-service with presenters on the topic of instructional intelligence strategies. They are closing the learning process with a team reflection.

**Rational Aim**
Decide on the instructional intelligence strategy or strategies that we will focus on to improve our instruction in support of our department or school-wide SMART goal.

**Experiential Aim**
Continue as a Professional Learning Community in our practice of collaborating in teams with the purpose of improving instruction and promoting school success.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Experience of in-service including presentation by Barrie Bennett

**Hints**
Having people connect a presenter's content to their own success at the reflective level is a good way to set the stage for accepting changes and improving their own behaviour.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
- Designate timekeeper.
- Designate minute-recorder.
- Designate minute-publisher (type-up & e-mail to department-optional)
- Share rational aim.
- Participants agree on norms for the collaboration.
- Set timeline for work for focused conversation.

**Objective Questions**
- What were the instructional strategies that we saw today?
- What were some of the points you recall from Barrie Bennett's presentation?

**Reflective Questions**
- What specific Instructional Intelligence strategies were you reminded of that you are already using in your classroom?
- How are you using these strategies?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What effects are these strategies having on student achievement?
- In what ways can we expand or refine our use of Instructional Intelligence strategies in our classrooms?

**Decisional Questions**
- Which Instructional Intelligence strategy or strategies will we focus on in our course teams (or our department team) to support our SMART goal?
- What final product do we want to produce in each team? What is our timeline for producing the product?

**Closing**
- Other thoughts?
- Minute taker reviews minutes with the group.

---

## 페이지 284 (SKU-000671170_11_00284.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition 271

## Conducting a meeting of an Individualized Placement and Review Committee (IPRC)

---

### 표 구성: Situation/Rational Aim/Experiential Aim/Concrete Beginning Point/Hints (좌측) | THE CONVERSATION (우측)

---

**Situation**
The parents of a severely handicapped, 8 year-old boy have come, with an advocate from a local association for disabled people, to plead for additional assistance and placement of their son in a fully integrated classroom, in the neighbourhood school. Due to financial constraints and limited availability of specially trained staff, the special education department of the regional school board is recommending placement in a segregated class of 8 students in another school some thirty minutes away from the student's home.

**Rational Aim**
To provide an educational program that meets the student's needs, within the available resources, and that is acceptable to the parents.

**Experiential Aim**
To establish an on-going, positive relationship among all those directly involved in the care and education of the student.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Clinical Information

**Hints**
Severe time limits on this conversation may make it seem that the decision has already been made before the meeting. It may be necessary to have a smaller, informal group explore to the options stage first and bring these to the formal meeting.

---

**THE CONVERSATION**

**Opening**
Welcome Mr. & Mrs. D. Thank you for coming and for bringing Ms W to lend her expertise in the discussion. I am F and with me are P, V, and Y. Ms G will be taking notes and you will receive a copy when they are distributed. Although this is a legally constituted meeting of the IPRC for Area 6 of our School Board, I hope that we can reach most, if not all, of our decisions by consensus, through relatively informal dialogue. Unfortunately, we do have other meetings scheduled so time is limited.

**Objective Questions**
- What clinical information do we have about Tim's situation?
- What are his educational needs? His personal care needs?
- What resources are required to meet Tim's needs while he is at school?
- What are his transportation needs?

**Reflective Questions**
- What continues to frustrate the family?...the teachers and resource personnel working with Tim? What successes have we had?

**Interpretive Questions**
- How might we build on our success?
- What resources are currently available and how can they be accessed?
- How might we obtain additional resources?
- What supporting data do we need? From whom? When?
- Where can the family obtain additional support?

**Decisional Questions**
- As a preferred choice, where will we place Tim and what resources are we able to provide?
- As a second choice, where will we place Tim and what resources are we able to provide?
- When can we confirm placement?
- How and when can the placement decision be appealed?
- What are our next steps?

*(continued)*

---

### Conducting a meeting of an Individualized Placement and Review Committee (IPRC) *(continued)*

|---|---|
| | Thank you for sharing the clinical information and for giving us the benefit of your special insight. We have covered a lot of very critical and detailed information and I thank everyone for the careful attention paid to the speakers. The decisions we have reached are tentative until the Committee has considered all of the students who will be presented this term. A final decision will be communicated by letter on (date) and I will be available to answer questions. |

## 페이지 286 (SKU-000671170_11_00286.jpeg)

# Format for New Kindergarten Report Card

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition* **273**

---

## Situation
The Kindergarten teachers across the school district want to create a common report card to be used in all schools. They have already identified the content for the report card and are ready to create the format. Samples of report cards have been gathered from around the province and country.

**Rational Aim**
To identify the format for a report card that will accurately reflect the curriculum and effectively communicate students' progress.

**Experiential Aim**
All staff will feel they have input into the creation of the report card and therefore support the implementation of the use of a common report card.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Samples of report cards

**Hints**
It will be very helpful to have parents involved during the creation of the report card instead of just at the end of the process. Note that all four levels of questions are given to the table groups in the opening section. This streamlines their thinking and prepares them for the large group conversation.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
Now that we know what we want in our report card, we can now look at the format the report card will take. Looking at the samples at your table ask yourself:
- What details catch your attention?
- What formats do you like?
- What do we need to add/delete?
- What do you want ours to look like? Layout? Checklist?
- What might be the main headings?

### Objective Questions
- As you looked at these formats, what catches your attention?
- What different elements do you see in the different samples?
- What comments have you heard from parents about report cards?
- What questions do you have for clarification?

### Reflective Questions
- What is your first reaction or response?
- Which of these formats have the most appeal? Least appeal?

### Interpretive Questions
- What key insight(s) have you had?
- What elements of these different formats will help us to effectively communicate student progress?

### Decisional Questions
- How should we organize these elements on our report card?

### Closing
We have done a lot of hard work here today, with everyone's input we have created a report card that is curriculum focused and organized in a way that we think will work for you as the teacher in accurately communicating student growth. Our next steps will be to build a prototype of the report card and then come back together to reflect on our work. Then we will be ready to take the report card to executive council and parent councils for their feedback.

---

## 페이지 287 (SKU-000671170_11_00287.jpeg)

# 274 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Lesson Design

### Situation
Teachers are planning for, and infusing higher order thinking skills into teaching and assessment activities at various grade levels. In subject/grade teams or small groups, teachers are working together to plan curriculum-based teaching & assessment activities to encourage higher order thinking.

### Rational Aim
To help teachers plan lessons that effectively engage students in their learning and move beyond recall of information, to make connections for deeper understanding of content.

### Experiential Aim
Bring conscious attention to planning for deeper learning by applying ORID as a tool in lesson design, as well as a process for reflecting on student learning.

### Concrete Beginning Point
Learning objectives for the curriculum and lessons

### Hints
The ORID format can be used in this way as an underlying structure to teach any topic while ensuring the use of higher order thinking skills. The ORID posters can be used on the classroom wall to help improve the structure of clear thinking. The learning placemat is useful for recording individual observation, reflection and insights (O & R), as well as for gathering data for group dialogue and team learning (I & D).

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
We're going to experiment with a format to help us create lesson plans that will encourage higher-order thinking in our students. Let's start by looking at the learning objectives for our curriculum and lesson.

### Objective Questions
What content knowledge, information, or skills do the objectives state that students are expected to know / be able to do?

What is the main learning outcome for this lesson?

### Reflective Questions
What personal reactions or emotions do we want students to experience during this activity / lesson / unit, that provide an emotional connection to knowledge or concept being presented? (for example empathy, admiration, outrage at a social injustice, etc., or feelings of satisfaction, increased confidence with progress in mastering a skill, meeting a goal, etc.)

### Interpretive Questions
How will students share, communicate and demonstrate their understanding of this concept to others?

### Decisional Questions
How might we have students apply this information in meaningful ways?

What actions or decisions might result from this learning / new skills / connections to new concepts?

### Closing
Choose one teaching or assessment activity to implement with students in the next few weeks. Use the ORID placemat to record your observations and personal reactions to students as they respond to the lesson. Bring a copy of the lesson and placemat to our next staff meeting, to share with colleagues.

---

## 페이지 288 (SKU-000671170_11_00288.jpeg)

# Peer Coaching Conversation to Enhance Professional Learning and Practice

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 275*

---

## 좌측 패널

**Situation**
Two teachers are collaborating to reflect on and plan effective lessons.

**Rational Aim**
To practice peer coaching skills for the purposes of meaningful reflection and effective planning.

**Experiential Aim**
To enhance the competency, craftsmanship and collaboration between the teachers as the "coaching" teacher becomes adept in applying effective interpersonal communication skills of paraphrasing, wait time, and questioning to mediate and activate the higher order thinking skills of her colleague.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Yesterday's lesson

**Hints**
In a coaching conversation, paraphrasing and wait time are critical to establishing rapport, and creating the space for meaningful reflection, and to access, surface and clarify one's thinking. Questions are typically open ended, and asked after a paraphrase, so as not to create a tone of "interrogation".

---

## THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
We're going to work together so I can practice my coaching skills and you can reflect on and plan your lesson...

**Objective Questions**
- What happened? / What did you observe?
- What did the students do?
- What did you do?
- What data/evidence did you collect?

**Reflective Questions**
- How do you feel it went?
- How do you know?
- What data/evidence do you have to support your impressions?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What comparisons have you made to other lessons? / this class?
- What conclusions would you draw?
- What do you know now that you didn't know then?
- What adaptations are you considering?

**Decisional Questions**
- What is your intention, objective, goal?
- What is uppermost for you to attend to?
- What steps will you take?
- What resources do you need?
- How will you know you are successful?

**Closing**
- How has this coaching conversation helped you?
- What feedback do you have for me, the "coach"?
- What might I do differently next time to assist you?

---

## 페이지 289 (SKU-000671170_11_00289.jpeg)

# Collaborative Analysis of Student Work

## 276 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

---

### Situation
- Department meeting focused on collaborative analysis of student work

### Rational Aim
Department members will gain insight into the value of collaboratively analyzing student work to effect changes in instructional practice.

### Experiential Aim
Department members will feel encouraged / motivated to try collaborative analysis of student work.

### Concrete Beginning Point
Article about examining student work

### Hints
Having working assumptions or group norms in place complemented by protocols for text-based discussions made explicit BEFORE beginning the conversation. Depending on the dynamic of the group, the department head may wish to be a participant and have an external facilitator lead the conversation.

### Other Applications
This could be used at elementary level for grade level team meetings or at the secondary level for course teams (i.e. a smaller group than a whole department)

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
We're going to read an article from a professional academic journal which addresses the process of examining student work as a group. After we've all had chance to read it, we'll have a conversation focused on 4 key questions. Feel free to make notes in the margin, underline ideas and/or highlight the text.

### Objective Questions
What specific word(s), phrase(s) or idea(s) caught your attention while you were reading?

### Reflective Questions
What is something in the article that makes you say an emphatic or enthusiastic "Yes!" in agreement? What is something about which you remain tentative, unsure or unclear?

### Interpretive Questions
Of the ideas in the article, which one(s) seem most easily achievable for you as an individual OR for us as a department? Which one(s) pose the greatest challenge?

### Decisional Questions
What are all the things we need to do as a department to make collaboration/analysis of student work a practical reality and/or a consistent practice? What ground rules / norms of collaboration do we need to adopt?

### Closing
Thanks for your active participation and frank insights.

---

## 페이지 290 (SKU-000671170_11_00290.jpeg)

# Math Curriculum Mapping Grades 6 to 8

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 277*

---

## Situation

A math consultant is working with a cross-panel group of teachers to support success in Grade 9 math by working consistently with students throughout Grades 6 to 9. The group first brainstormed all the tasks students had to do in grade 9, then had a conversation to analyze that data. (See "Grade 9 Task Analysis".) This conversation goes into more detail, starting with curriculum mapped across the grades, to understand how they can work with the curriculum to support students.

**Rational Aim:** To develop a common understanding of how the 6-8 curriculum supports students to be successful in the grade 9 math tasks we have just analyzed.

**Shared Knowledge Aim:** The shared knowledge of the grade 6-8 curriculum and grade 9 tasks will enable us to identify concepts, knowledge, skills and processes, areas of student performances and mathematical thinking that are challenging, that are well-connected, and that are well-connected for students across grades 6-9.

**Experiential Aim:** To share in the commitment to ensure that our students learn deeply, feel capable of learning and are motivated to continue learning.

**Concrete Beginning Point:** Math Curriculum Map across grades

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening

In the previous conversation we identified what we must be "doing" in our classrooms in order for students to experience success in grade 9. Next, it is important for us to understand how the curriculum across grades 6 to 8 supports students to be successful in grade 9 tasks. I have created a curriculum mapping of expectations across grades 6 to 8 in the *(insert strand name)* strand, organized and aligned by topic across each of the grades. Let's take 10 minutes to view the mapping. As you view the mapping, keep in mind what was learned through the grade 9 task analysis.

### Objective Questions
- What does the map say about **What are students learning?**
- What does the map say about **How are students learning it?**
- What does the map say about **What students will be "doing"** while they are learning?

### Reflective Questions
- What aligns with your thinking?
- What concerns do you have?
- Where will our students struggle?
- Where will our students experience success?

### Interpretive Questions
- What concepts, skills and mathematical thinking will be critical to support success in the grade 9 tasks?
- What is "worth being familiar with" or not so important to success in grade 9 mathematics?
- Where is the curriculum well-connected across the grades to support success in these grade 9 tasks?
- Where is the curriculum not well-connected across the grades to support success in these grade 9 tasks?

### Decisional Questions
- Given what we have learned, what must we commit to do as a cross panel team to support success in mathematics across grades 6 to 9?

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 291 (SKU-000671170_11_00291.jpeg)

# 278 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Math Curriculum Mapping Grades 6 to 8 *(continued)*

| | **Closing** |
|---|---|
| | You have identified ways in which our grades 6 to 8 curriculum supports students to be successful and ways in which you will reframe the intention of the expectations in light of our cross grade and cross panel understanding of what is important for students to know, do and understand. Thank you for sharing in the commitment to ensure that our students learn deeply, feel capable of learning and are motivated to continue learning. |

## 페이지 292 (SKU-000671170_11_00292.jpeg)

# Meeting Deadlines

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 279*

---

## 좌측 패널

**Situation**
A colleague is consistently unable to make deadlines for the completion of or submission of work (reports, etc.)

**Rational Aim**
To resolve the issue of unmanageable deadlines by determining effective and manageable coping strategies

**Experiential Aim**
To feel that a mutually agreeable resolution to the problem was arrived at in a respectful and professional manner.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Recent deadlines and behaviour in relation to them

**Hints**
It is important for the person who is unable to make the deadlines to feel that while some pressure is being exerted that there is a recognition of the difficulties that making deadlines causes. The matter needs to be handled sensitively as well as directly.

**Other Applications**
This conversation can be adapted for any circumstance in which a person is not meeting job expectations.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
*(요약)* 마감일 관련 상황을 논의하고자 하며, 마감을 불가능한 것이 아닌 관리 가능한 것으로 만드는 방법에 집중하고자 함.

### Objective Questions
- What are some deadlines that we've had recently?
- What have you observed about our ability to meet deadlines in the recent past?

### Reflective Questions
- When you hear the word "deadline", what associations (words, pictures, emotions) do you immediately make?
- What was a positive experience you had with a deadline?
- What was a negative experience you had with a deadline?

### Interpretive Questions
- What is currently and preventing us from consistently meeting critical deadlines?
- What new/different steps might/could we realistically and practically take to help us set and meet future deadlines?
- Which of these steps is easiest to accomplish?
- Which of these steps poses the greatest challenge to accomplish?

### Decisional Questions
- What protocol or process WILL we put in place to ensure that we set reasonable deadlines and meet them?

### Closing
*(요약)* 마감일에 대한 생각을 공유해 주셔서 감사하며, 실질적인 전략을 파악하고 향후 의무를 이행할 수 있을 것으로 기대함.

---

## 페이지 293 (SKU-000671170_11_00293.jpeg)

# Content for New Report Card

## Situation
The Kindergarten teachers across the school district want to create a common report card to be used in all schools. A few years back the Kindergarten teachers had come together to identify the critical learnings or "big ideas" of the English Language arts curriculum.

**Rational Aim**
To identify the content for a report card that would accurately reflect the curriculum and effectively communicate students' progress.

**Experiential Aim**
All staff will feel they have input into the creation of the report card and therefore support the implementation of the use of a common report card.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Kindergarten curriculum and "big ideas" of language arts previously identified

**Hints**
The big ideas in English Language Arts are helpful because the teachers are able to use these to clearly articulate what early literacy looks like at the Kindergarten level quite quickly.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
Before we begin to look at the format for your report card let's individually skim through the Kindergarten curriculum and remind ourselves of what is in it, as well as the "big ideas" of the English language arts curriculum you identified several years ago. Ask yourself:
- What elements do we need to report?
- What other areas besides language arts?
- Basically, what do you need/want to report on in the report card?

### Objective Questions
As you skimmed through this curriculum and your identified "big ideas" what were the key concepts/elements for reporting on a report card?

What else needs to be included?

### Reflective Questions
What concerns you?

What parts are you okay with?

### Interpretive Questions
What categories do you see emerging?

### Decisional Questions
Would these categories include everything you want to see on the report card? What else would you add?

How will these categories reflect the critical elements of the provincial Program of Studies for Kindergarten?

What need to be changed or added?

### Closing
Now that we have identified the content for your report card our next steps will be to identify a format that will be both practical for you as the teacher and easy to understand for parents.

---

## 페이지 294 (SKU-000671170_11_00294.jpeg)

# Talking with a Parent at a Parent/Teacher Conference

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition* **281**

---

## 왼쪽 패널

**Situation**
High school teachers are preparing for parent/teacher conferences. A colleague gives them this template to help them all have more productive conversations.

**Rational Aim**
To share information on student performance

**Experiential Aim**
To establish mutual respect and trust, and commitment to supporting the student's best learning.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Child's Report card

**Hints**
This conversation was adapted from p. 203-4 and augmented to fit a real high school situation. This is a very good example of how to use the templates in the book and CD.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Let's look at some information on your son/daughter's progress this term.

**Objective Questions**
- Here is some data from my mark book. What clarification do you need about this information?
- What would you add?
- What comments have you heard from John about his studies in my class?
- As you look through his report, what do you notice? What catches your eye?

**Reflective Questions**
- What pleases you most about how John is doing?
- What worries you?
- What surprises you?
- What specific concerns do you have about this detailed report?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What does this tell you about John's work for the first half of this semester?
- What do you think might be underlying reasons for this?
- What are major opportunities or concerns we might need to address?
- What would like to see by the end of this semester?

**Decisional Questions**
- What are some things we can do to get there?
- In which areas can we work most effectively together?
- Where do we need to improve?
- What can we do to support and encourage John's highest possible achievement?
- What do we need to do to make sure that John's educational goals are met?
- What else can I do to assist you?
- What do we need to do over the remainder of this semester?

**Closing**
Thank you very much for coming out tonight. With both of us working together to support John, I am certain we can help him do better.

---

## 페이지 295 (SKU-000671170_11_00295.jpeg)

# 282 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Teacher-Parent Conflict over Level of Student Assistance Provided

### Situation
A single mother telephones the principal, complaining that her 10-year-old daughter's teacher is not providing the additional assistance promised at the last parent-teacher interview. She tells the principal that her daughter has been having a lot of difficulty with her schoolwork and is becoming increasingly difficult to manage at home. She also mentions that her daughter visits her father every second weekend and on some holidays.

**Rational Aim**
To determine the student's needs and the level of additional assistance required.

**Experiential Aim**
To establish mutual respect and trust, and commitment to supporting the student's best learning.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Jennifer's observed behaviour

**Hints**
Although it is important to acknowledge the frustration and anxiety/resentment expressed by the parties in the discussion, it is equally important that no one go away with the impression that everything has been resolved when, in fact, it hasn't. Like a good physician, it is important that teachers project a hopeful attitude yet be completely honest. At all costs, sure cures are to be avoided.

*(continued)*

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Thank you Mrs. A. for calling me; and Mr. T. for suggesting that we meet to discuss the various concerns. We all want Jennifer (student) to be successful in her schoolwork and that she will become a happier person. As I see it, we are all here today to find ways to help each other and help Jennifer.

**Objective Questions**
- What are some of Jennifer's behaviours around schoolwork you are observing at home?
- What are you observing in class?
- What are some of the other background factors in Jennifer's life that may be relevant?

**Reflective Questions**
- What does Jennifer do that causes you the greatest frustration?
- What does Jennifer do that gives you the most satisfaction?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What are the limits to what you are personally able to do to assist Jennifer?
- What other factors do you think might be contributing to Jennifer's difficulties?
- What do each of you think Jennifer needs most?
- How have been addressing these needs in class? At home?
- What more does Jennifer need?
- How do you interpret Jennifer's reactions to your efforts to help her?
- How does Jennifer try to deal with her difficulties?
- What seems to motivate Jennifer most? Why?
- What does Jennifer resent most? Why?

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 296 (SKU-000671170_11_00296.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition 283

## Teacher-Parent Conflict over Level of Student Assistance Provided *(continued)*

| **Other Applications** | **Decisional Questions** |
|---|---|
| These episodes can be a great source of heuristic case studies for later use in professional development exercises. They can become, in fact, the scripts for role plays. Better still, with everyone's permission and enthusiastic participation, the actual meetings could be video taped for use in limited professional development exercises. This calls for a very high level of trust and scrupulous adherence to the terms of the agreement. | What is it that each of us is prepared to do, to help Jennifer? How best can we communicate with each other? How should we involve Jennifer in what we are planning to do? Who else can become constructively involved? What other sources of assistance should we be considering? Who will do what? By when? When do we review our efforts and the results? |

### Closing

We have listed a number of Jennifer's needs and there seems to be agreement on those I've marked with an asterisk. Should I make any changes? Are there others? Thank you, both, for participating in this activity. I hope this meeting will get us closer to providing Jennifer with the help that she needs immediately; and will identify other sources and strategies we can use in the future. I look forward to our next meeting.

---

## 페이지 297 (SKU-000671170_11_00297.jpeg)

# Parents' Group Responses to New Report Card

*284 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS*

---

## Situation
After a year of work, a new draft report card has been created with input from across the district. A committee has a draft that they are nearly ready to implement. They want parents' feedback on what parents think for final finesse before implementation.

**Rational Aim**
To gather parents' responses to the new report card

**Experiential Aim**
To provide parents with an avenue to respond to the new report card draft

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Sample Report Card

**Hints**
Be very clear in the context about the level of participation you are asking for in this conversation. This conversation is not asking the group to make a decision, nor for input for the project to start all over. When people know on what level they are being asked to contribute, their participation is more honest and helpful. Someone else besides the facilitator needs to answer the questions of clarification so that the facilitator maintains their neutral stance.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
Parents are the prime audience for report cards. Report cards are a tool to communicate your students' achievement to you. Therefore, we value your opinions on how these report cards communicate to you. We have a draft that has been created from much input. We're almost ready to roll it out but we want your input for the finessing of the final version.

### Objective Questions
- What is the first thing that catches your attention on this report card?
- What are the key phrases in the different scales for reporting achievement, effort and Personal and Social Growth (PSG)?
- What strikes you about the Achievement, Effort, and PSG scales?
- What do you notice about how student achievement is reported?
- What questions of clarification do you have of the committee?

### Reflective Questions
- What is familiar or comfortable for you about this report card?
- What are you unsure about in this report card?
- What concerns you about this report card?

### Interpretive Questions
- How are the scales similar to those you know?
- What is different from what you know?
- What would be some of the impacts of this report card upon students – both positive and negative?
- What messages does this report card give you?
- What questions do you have that need to be clarified if this report card is used?

### Decisional Questions
- What in this report card works for you?
- What in this report card doesn't work for you?
- What else do you need to make this work?

### Closing
Your feedback as parents will be taken into account in drafting a final, finished version of the report cards for use in Regina Public Schools. Thank you for your thoughtfulness in participation today!

---

## 페이지 298 (SKU-000671170_11_00298.jpeg)

# Processing New Information

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition* 285

---

## Processing New Information

| **Situation** | **THE CONVERSATION** |
|---|---|

**Situation**
Staff members are considering ways to address the needs of struggling readers. After reading the article entitled Profiles of Comprehension (Applegate, M. D., Quinn, K. B., & Applegate, A. J. (2006). Profiles in Comprehension, The Reading Teacher, 60, 48-67), they share their understandings, process the information, and decide how they might use this particular system of programming for students.

**Rational Aim**
To understand the various "profiles of comprehension" and use that information to assess, evaluate, and program for student learning.

**Experiential Aim**
To feel intrigued with the possibilities of a new way to analyze student reading performance.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Article "Profiles of Comprehension"

---

### Opening
Let's read this article, think about new learnings and possible applications for our work in the classroom.

### Objective Questions
- What are the key features of each profile?
- What are the interventions for each profile?
- What information stood out for you?

### Reflective Questions
- What appeals to you?
- What are you skeptical about?

### Interpretive Questions
- What might be the impact of this system of classifications on the students?
- How might this system of classifications support you in your work with the students?
- What might be the greatest challenge to you in applying this system of classifications?

### Decisional Questions
- When might you use this system of classifications?
- How might you prepare to use this system?

### Closing
Thank you for the fun of exploring the insight in this article. I intend to use some of our ideas in my own teaching.

---

## 페이지 299 (SKU-000671170_11_00299.jpeg)

# 286 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Reflecting on Successes

### 상황/구성 정보 (왼쪽 열)

**Situation**
A group of teachers in a staff meeting rarely have a chance to do anything but solve problems together. The principal decides to spend a session highlighting and learning from success.

**Rational Aim**
To identify factors in successful student learning in order to build on these positive experiences.

**Experiential Aim**
Pride and confidence from shared successes to move forward

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Shared stories of success

**Hints**
Encourage listening to each person's story all the way through without interruption, to acknowledge them fully.

**Other Applications**
This can be used with any topic where you want to build on success: for example, with school secretaries who need to see the strong role they play on the administration team to foster student success.

---

### THE CONVERSATION (오른쪽 열)

**Opening**
We have many things that we are doing successfully that we rarely have an opportunity to share and learn from each other on. Let's take a few minutes to share some successes with each other, whether small or large.

Go around the group: Each person tell a quick story about something you've done in your classroom that worked really well, where a student (or students) were successful in learning.

**Objective Questions**
After each story: Any questions of clarification about this story?

**Reflective Questions**
What was most exciting or inspiring about any one of these stories?

**Interpretive Questions**
What impact do any of these have on student learning?

Why?

Out of these stories, what would you say are some important factors in promoting student learning? *(List what people answer.)*

**Decisional Questions**
How might you apply any of what you've learned here in your own classroom?

**Closing**
*(Thank the group for their wisdom.)*

---

## 페이지 300 (SKU-000671170_11_00300.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition 287

## Resolving a Conflict between Teachers about Responsibility for Managing Student Behaviour

### [표/도해 요약]

**Situation:** 4학년 남학생 Jonas가 도서관에서 문제를 일으킴. 사서와 담임교사가 각각 상대방의 "비전문성"을 교장에게 불만 제기.

**Rational Aim:** 도서관에서 학생 "연구"를 위한 기준 재정립. 책임 소재 명확화.

**Experiential Aim:** 전문적 협력과 효과적 문제해결 정신 함양.

**Concrete Beginning Point:** Jonas의 도서관 사건.

**Hints:** 어느 한쪽을 "blame frame"에 두지 말 것. 학생의 필요에 집중할 것.

**Other Applications:** 도서관, 체육관 등 공유 자원을 포함한 관리 문제 논의에 활용 가능.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening:** Jonas와 도서관 사건에 대해 논의. 두 분 모두 매우 좌절하고 속상해하심을 앎. 서로 협력하여 Jonas의 필요를 이해하고 도울 방법 모색.

**Objective Questions** / **Reflective Questions** / **Interpretive Questions** / **Decisional Questions** 포함.

**Closing:** Jonas의 필요와 오해의 원인에 대한 더 나은 이해. 향후 follow-up 제안.

---

## 페이지 301 (SKU-000671170_11_00301.jpeg)

# 288 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Revising the School Effectiveness Plan

### Situation
Teams are reviewing data and revising the school effectiveness plan. A think-pair-share process is used to look at the discrete pieces of data. Then they look at the data as a whole division.

**Rational Aim**
The group will have analyzed school achievement data and set school goals for literacy, numeracy, and culture/climate, with next steps to achieve them, as a school effectiveness plan.

**Experiential Aim**
Teachers will be committed to improving school effectiveness.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Student Achievement Data

**Hints**
There may be a lot of conversation triggered around the last interpretive questions and the decisional questions, as they may not have simple, obvious answers. The challenge will be to keep it on topic while the conversation opens up, and then to bring it back to closure. It may be necessary to break into small groups and use a simple ORID format for each to probe obstacles and effective strategies to reach the goals.

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
As a division, we need to review the data on our students...

**Objective Questions**
- What catches your attention?
- What points do you need clarity on?
- What is your first reaction?
- What surprises you?
- What professional knowledge do you associate with this data?

**Reflective Questions**
- What is your first reaction?
- What surprises you?
- What professional knowledge do you associate with this data?

**Interpretive Questions**
- Which aspects of this data are most important for you? Our division? Why?
- What trends do you see emerging from this data?
- What does this tell you about how well we're meeting our goals – literacy, numeracy, school climate?
- What changes might be required from us?
- Which needs to be dealt with first? Why?

**Decisional Questions**
- What shall we set as our Literacy goal? Our Numeracy goal? Our Culture/Climate goal?
- How shall we go about meeting these goals?
- What is our first step? Second? Who should do it?

**Closing**
These are important decisions and will help us make a difference in our school effectiveness plan. Thank you for your wisdom and commitment.

---

# School Goal Planning for Aboriginal Education

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 289*

---

## Situation
School Learning Council: A workshop is being held with administrators from a range of schools in the district to share goals and progress on Aboriginal education.

## Rational Aim
Acquire a sense of how schools are progressing towards their goals for Aboriginal education and how we are understanding the meaning of Aboriginal education.

## Experiential Aim
To deepen our understanding. To share and learn from our experience.

## Concrete Beginning Point
A presentation on demographics and context for Aboriginal education.

## Hints
If this is a group of more than 25 people, put the questions on a flipchart and allow small groups to have simultaneous conversations.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
- Working Assumptions and Agreements
- We must expect and accept that we will not reach closure.
- Introductions

### Objective Questions
- What catches your attention in the information presented?
- What questions of clarity do you have?
- What do you need more information about?

### Reflective Questions
- What surprises you in this information?
- How does it compare with your own intuitive sense or personal knowledge about the situation?
- What most concerns you or makes you feel anxious? Where are you struggling?
- What makes you feel hopeful?

### Interpretive Questions
- What does Aboriginal education look like and sound like in your school?
- What impact can Aboriginal education have for Aboriginal students? For non-Aboriginal students? For our whole community and our shared future?
- What hurdles and challenges do you see?
- What strengths and assets can you draw on?

### Decisional Questions
- What is a useful working definition of Aboriginal education in your school?

*(continued)*

What are some next steps for you personally?

**Closing**

Building a shared future for our community is a lifelong struggle. We are taking responsibility and positive/creative action towards achieving this vision for our children and ourselves.

What have we done here this PM? What was surprising, exciting or frustrating?

What have we learned? How will we use what we have learned back in our schools?

## 페이지 304 (SKU-000671170_11_00304.jpeg)

# Reflection on Year's School Improvement Project

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 291*

---

## Left Column

**Situation**
A principal requested a facilitated reflective conversation on the school improvements staff had completed over the year, to model the process as a tool for the school leadership team and staff to use to reflect on the year and to begin planning for the upcoming term.

**Rational Aim**
To reflect on the school's Instructional Focus work, set direction for the next term and provide input to the leadership staff for future planning.

**Experiential Aim**
To appreciate the successes and challenges of all staff. To continue to develop capacity for shared leadership through using a new reflective tool.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Shared experience of actions in the past year.

**Hints**
The process helps strengthen and deepen conversation around a topic (seeing multi viewpoints) and clarify paths to decision-making.

**Other Applications**
Can be used for other projects where learning and growth are needed. It is a tool for a learning community which acts, reflects on its actions, learns from the experience, and changes behaviour.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
We're going to use a "Focused Conversation Process" to help us think clearly as a group about the past year. This reflection is designed to help us to learn from our successes and struggles and determine the best way to move forward.

**Objective Questions**
- What are some of the things you have done to move the work forward at the school level?
- What are some of the major things you have done in your classroom to move the work forward?

**Reflective Questions**
- What successes have you achieved that you are proud of?
- What worries you about the work ahead?
- If you were to compare the work to a circus visual image what comes to mind and why? (E.g., clowning, juggling; candy floss, candy apples, etc.)

**Interpretive Questions**
- What have been the most significant factors in moving the work forward in your school? In your classroom?
- What evidence of student growth have you seen?
- What alternatives are important to consider to move the work ahead?

**Decisional Questions**
- What do you consider most important in continuing the work next year? At school, or for yourself?
- What are your priorities for next year?
- What do you need your Leadership Team to do to facilitate and support your work?

**Closing**
Recalling the process we used today, what did you notice in your thinking and reflecting? What was a highlight in your experience of the process? What did you struggle with?

- Where else in your work are reflections important?
- Where might you use the process?

---

## 페이지 305 (SKU-000671170_11_00305.jpeg)

# 292 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Child's/Student's Academic Progress

### Situation
A teacher is the parent of a student in a parent-teacher interview, guiding the conversation with their child's teacher.

### Rational Aim
Both the teacher and the parents will additional insight into strengths, areas for improvement and next steps for a student/child

### Experiential Aim
Both teacher and parents will feel satisfied having a frank conversation about the progress about the student/child

### Concrete Beginning Point
Observations of student

### Hints
*(지도 방법에 대한 힌트 포함)*

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
I wanted to gather any insights you may have about _______ progress. One of the things we both know is that kids behave differently at home than they do at school. So, we wanted to ascertain whether your observations mirrored ours at home. This will, in turn, help all of us to support _______ in his/her studies

### Objective Questions
What have you observed about _______ as a student in your class (e.g. behaviour/interaction with peers, level of engagement, focus on task, work completion, skills,etc.)?

### Reflective Questions
What pleases you about _______ as a student?
What concerns you about him/her as a student?

### Interpretive Questions
What are some things _______ could work on in terms of learning skills or curriculum expectations to continue growing and developing as a learner?

### Decisional Questions
Collectively, what do you, as his/her teacher, we, as his/her parents, and he/she, as the student, need to do to ensure that he/she continues to excel, remains engaged, and still feels challenged in and at school?

### Closing
Thanks for both your candor and insights and for taking time to call/meet with me/us. We feel better prepared to help him/her in his/her studies.

---

## 페이지 306 (SKU-000671170_11_00306.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition 293

## Summer Staff Decision about Quitting

---

**Situation**
A location supervisor of a children's camp approaches you about a staff member in their program that is thinking of quitting. They have already approached the staff and cannot get a sense of the staff's direction. They ask you to speak to the staff person to help them decide what they will do next.

**Rational Aim**
Create discussion that will ultimately help the staff member decide whether they will continue to work or leave their position.

**Experiential Aim**
The staff member will experience a supportive investigatory discussion about their future employment.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Staff Person's Experience

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
I have been told by your supervisor that you may be uncertain about working in this program. I am here to support you in whatever decision you decide. Let's talk about your experiences in this job.

**Objective Questions**
- What are the important experiences you have had in this job?
- What parts of this experience stand out?

**Reflective Questions**
- What words, behaviors situations stand out in your mind about your experience?
- What parts of this job do you like the most?
- What parts are most challenging?
- How do you feel about your job?
- What has surprised you about this experience?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What have you learned about yourself from this experience?
- How this experience fit (or not fit) with your goals?

**Decisional Questions**
- What is the next step for you in this experience?

**Closing**
I hope this discussion has helped you to decide what to do next. If I can be of any further help please contact me.

---

## 페이지 307 (SKU-000671170_11_00307.jpeg)

# 294 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Supporting Camp Supervisor

### Situation
The camp supervisor comes to you for support and direction on how they should approach the issue of staff communication.

**Rational Aim**
This conversation is designed to help a supervisor to understand the steps necessary to address communication issues with staff.

**Experiential Aim**
Supervisor will experience a supportive discussion that allows them to feel confident in approaching the staff team.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Supervisor experiences with staff

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Thanks for meeting with me. Let's have a discussion about the issues you are facing with your staff team.

**Objective Questions**
- What behaviour or words do you see and hear from your staff?
- What interactions do you see happening with the staff team?

**Reflective Questions**
- What experiences have surprised you?
- What positive or negative situations can you remember?
- What concerns you most about your staff team's level of communication?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What do you think are some of the root issues behind these communication issues?
- What do you think you can do to address issues of communication?
- What other supports are necessary to improve this situation?

**Decisional Questions**
- What will be your next step to address these issues?
- What must you do to involve the staff team in these solutions?
- What is the time line for these issues to be addressed?

**Closing**
I hope this discussion was productive for you. I think you have a good grasp on the situation. If I can be more assistance please contact me.

---

## 페이지 308 (SKU-000671170_11_00308.jpeg)

# Supportive Staff Interactions

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 295*

---

## Situation

At a staff meeting, the teachers and staff need to reach an agreement on ethical and professional behaviour that is in the best interests of children and will help bond the staff in developing a collegial and supportive approach in working as a team. They work in a very diverse, multi-cultural school in which addressing the needs of students can be very stressful. They are a very large staff, who have recently been critical of each other, including some staff reactions that were not as professional due to high stress. The principal wants them to be consistent in their approaches for children and in the way they interact as a staff.

**Rational Aim**
The group will identify ways they can support each other in times of differed opinions and in high stress situations.

**Experiential Aim**
The group will recognize desired professional behaviours and work to develop consistent ways they can support others. The group will become a closer team if this aim is accomplished. Consistent approaches among staff will result in best practices for children.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Examples of adult behaviours that affect students negatively

*(continued)*

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
*(요약)* 진정한 팀으로서 전문적 학습 공동체 성장, 안전한 환경 구축, 동료 간 열린 대화의 중요성 강조

### Objective Questions
- 이 학교가 아니더라도 아이들에게 최선이 아닌 행동/행위 사례 생각해보기

### Reflective Questions
- 그런 행동을 목격했을 때 어떤 느낌이었나?
- 이런 행동들이 가장 걱정되는 점은?
- 스태프로서 우리에게 어떤 영향을 미치나?

### Interpretive Questions
- 이런 행동들의 배경 요인은?
- 이런 행동이 발생할 때 우리가 할 수 있는 것은?
- 동료로서 서로 어떻게 도울 수 있나?
- 개인적으로 효과적인 방법은?

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 309 (SKU-000671170_11_00309.jpeg)

# 296 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Supportive Staff Interactions *(continued)*

| Hints | Decisional Questions |
|-------|---------------------|
| Record the staff answers on chart paper, especially the actions. A staff may be somewhat hesitant to begin this conversation. Giving a few examples and speaking about general behaviour, not just specific to the staff, may open communication. | **What do we need to do to ensure that this happens?** What actions will we agree to take to make this a more comfortable process? We're looking for what is good, fair and right. **Closing** I thank you for being so open in this conversation. I would like to check in with you in a few months to see how things are going. |

---

## 페이지 310 (SKU-000671170_11_00310.jpeg)

# Year-End Review of Transitions Program

*Additional Conversations from Second Edition 297*

---

## [표/도해 요약]

**Situation (상황)**
- 팀 멤버의 제안으로 특별 교육팀이 연간 전환 과정을 돌아보고, 해온 일을 깊이 검토하며 다음 해를 위한 결정을 내리기 위해 회의

**Rational Aim:** 지난해 경험을 바탕으로 다음 해 전환 프로그램 계획 수립

**Experiential Aim:** 어려움을 인정하고, 진행 중인 것을 확인하며, 미래에 대한 희망 갖기

**Concrete Beginning Point:** 전환 팀에서의 올해 경험

**Hints:** 그룹이 과거 학습을 통해 미래 행동을 구축하는 학습 그룹이 될 수 있게 하는 단순하지만 효과적인 대화

---

## THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Let's think about the transitioning process we experience this year and gather our collective wisdom.

**Objective Questions**
As you look back at transition meetings what memories stand out?

**Reflective Questions**
Where did we struggle?

**Interpretive Questions**
What should be the major purpose or outcome of a transition? Why do we transition the way we do? What are the key issues and problem areas?

**Decisional Questions**
What changes to the transitional process would you recommend?

**Closing**
This is great stuff. I'll document it and we'll work out the details in the fall. Have a great summer!

---

## 페이지 311 (SKU-000671170_11_00311.jpeg)

# Understanding the Key Principles of Backward Design (Curriculum Planning Model)

**298 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS**

---

## Situation
The consultant has been asked to help a group of teachers improve their curriculum planning process. He is using an article to inspire the group.

**Rational Aim**
Participants will have a firm grasp of the key principles of the "design down" model of curriculum design.

**Experiential Aim**
Participants will feel more confident about adopting this method more consistently in their own teaching practice.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Article on "Backward Design"

**Hints**
Using an article as concrete starting point helps to illuminate the theory and rationale for the use of this curriculum planning model. To extend the theory into practice, a companion (subsequent) ORID/focused conversation may prove useful. In a second conversation, using a sample lesson/unit as a concrete starting point helps to emphasize what a lesson/unit actually looks like. Offering two contrasting lesson/units may further reinforce why the process is so valuable.

**Other Applications**
This conversation can be adapted to deal with any instructional or assessment process/initiative which offers a competing or alternative model to one in common use or practice.

---

## THE CONVERSATION

### Opening
To help demystify the "why" and context for UbD or Backward design process (theory), we're going to read an article from ASCD's Educational Leadership journal called "Backward design for forward action". It has been truncated to remove material not directly related to our work. You may wish to use a highlighter as you read and there is a Scribble section at the article for any notes you may like to make. Afterwards, we'll have a conversation together.

### Objective Questions
What words, phrases or statements leapt off the page or resonated with you? (Please direct our attention to the article and quote from it directly)

### Reflective Questions
What did you find appealing or exhilarating about what you read? (In a moment, I'll ask what left you perplexed or confused.)

What did you find perplexing or a source of confusion?

### Interpretive Questions
What is a key insight or implication, raised by the article, for you as a classroom teacher?

### Decisional Questions
What key steps do you need to take to make this theory a practical reality in your course/lesson planning regimen?

### Closing
Thanks to every participant for offering your insights which emerged from the reading and for sharing your curriculum planning and classroom practices with us. The dialogue enriched our individual and collective understanding of the backward design model. I'd like to harness those elements and move from theory to practical applications.

---

## 페이지 312 (SKU-000671170_11_00312.jpeg)

# Additional Conversations from Second Edition 299

## Working Out Religious and Cultural Objections to a Swim Program

### Situation
As a result of the accidental drowning of a student on a school excursion, a swim program has been incorporated into the regular physical education schedule for grades 1-6. When Muslim families moved into the area, a problem arises with respect to the participation of their young daughters in the swim program. The families object to their daughters swimming in the presence of older boys and male instructors. The principal calls a meeting of interested families.

**Rational Aim**
To find an acceptable strategy that will allow the older female students to participate in the swim program.

**Experiential Aim**
Members of the different ethno-cultural groups in the school community will experience that they have influence on decisions affecting their children, and satisfaction with the solution.

**Concrete Beginning Point**
Description of the swim program, and concerns

**Hints**
Resolving cultural differences often requires prolonged discussion and periods of trial and error until something mutually satisfactory can be devised. There are many questions in this conversation—use only the minimum needed at each level.

*(continued)*

---

### THE CONVERSATION

**Opening**
Good evening ladies and gentlemen. Thank you for coming tonight, on such short notice. With me, to describe the swim program and answer questions, are the two teachers in charge of the program and the school nurse. We have a learn-to-swim program in our school, as a response to an accidental drowning of one of our students a few years ago. I have been informed that a number of families plan to exclude their older daughters from the program for religious and cultural reasons.

Let's first get a bit of clarification on what goes on in the learn-to-swim program. Would the teachers outline the practices and procedures employed in the swim program?

**Objective Questions**
- What questions of clarification do you have?
- Would someone describe, for the benefit of those of us who are unfamiliar with the cultural background, what are some of the expectations you have of young girls?
- What other relevant information would anyone else like to contribute?

**Reflective Questions**
- What bothers you most about the swim program as it is presently being offered?
- What conflicting feelings do we have around this issue?

**Interpretive Questions**
- What experience has anyone here had in resolving similar problems?
- Where can we look for guidance around issues like this?
- What is keeping us apart?
- What is pulling us together?
- What are the concerns we need to address?
- What are some of the options we have?
- What are the pros and cons of each of these options?

*(continued)*

---

## 페이지 313 (SKU-000671170_11_00313.jpeg)

# 300 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## Working Out Religious and Cultural Objections to a Swim Program *(continued)*

---

**[좌측 열]**

The facilitator needs to be aware of his or her own biases, and strongly maintain an open atmosphere to come up with a mutually satisfactory solution. Maintaining respect for all points of view, especially when a viable solution is slipping away through frustration, is the real test.

**Other Applications**

Looking for a range of possible solutions often prompts some creative adaptations. (In the real-life situation this conversation came from, the solution of wearing an oversized dark t-shirt over swimsuits was suggested by an older Muslim woman, and reinforced by the school nurse who said she herself did that because she felt more comfortable.)

---

**[우측 열]**

### Decisional Questions

- What changes could we make to the way(s) in which we conduct the swim program?
- How can we overcome the concerns?
- How can we strengthen the things that are working?
- What do we do next?
- How will we evaluate and communicate the results?

### Closing

This discussion has been very informative and I hope that we all have a better appreciation how this issue is perceived by all the parties concerned. It looks as if we have the beginning of a solution. With everyone's goodwill and patience I am sure we will overcome the barriers and all our children will benefit.

---

## LESSON DESIGN and Collaborative Sharing and Reflections for Personal Learning

**Lesson:** _______________
**Name:** _______________
**Lesson (Grade & Subject):** _______________
**Date:** _______________

---

### [표/도해 요약: DIOR 반성 프레임워크]

4개의 사분면으로 구성된 반성 도구:

**O (Observe/관찰)** - 오른쪽 상단
> What did you OBSERVE (teachers) in student behavior as they responded to the lesson? In their tasks or classwork?

**R (Reactions/반응)** - 오른쪽 하단
> What REACTIONS come to mind (feelings/ associations/questions) as you consider student responses to, or engagement in the activities?

**D (Decisions/결정)** - 왼쪽 하단
> What DECISIONS do you need to make regarding steps to design future lessons?

**I (Implications/함의)** - 왼쪽 상단
> What are the IMPLICATIONS (insights/activities) for student learning?

**Back Mirror** *(왼쪽 여백 텍스트)*

## 페이지 315 (SKU-000671170_11_00315.jpeg)

# 302 THE ART OF FOCUSED CONVERSATION FOR SCHOOLS

## A FOCUS ON LEARNING

**표/도해 요약: ORID 대화 프레임워크 (4분면 구성)**

| 구분 | 질문 |
|------|------|
| **O** (Objective) | What stands out for you? |
| **R** (Reflective) | What is your reaction to the chart? How do you think your staff might react? How might your parents react? |
| **I** (Interpretive) | If the culture of your school shifted to being obsessed about learning, what are the implications for practice? |
| **D** (Decisional) | How might you approach this conversation with teachers? ...parents? ...students? |

---

| **I = INTERPRETIVE - Implications** | *What did you see here today?* |
| **R = REFLECTIVE - Reactions** | *What are your reactions?* |
| **D = DECISIONAL - Directions** | *What would you change?* |
